side and salvation on the other. another touch of the girl’s lip would

have send they both into what the sensitive and honourable gentleman

would have call the abyss. perhaps, if she have be old, a woman,

one tune to the pulsate responsibility of life, he might have face

thing with she. who know? to his direct mind the casuistical point do

not occur. actuality alone concern he. she be so delicate and

fragrant a flower of girlhood. his for the plucking. . . . when he

regain his college room, that far-off summer afternoon, he be as a

man tear by devil. love she? he would be tear in piece rather than

that her exquisite foot should be bruise against a stone. love she?

with her soft voice, her madden Madonna face, her kind eye, her

tremulous mouth? love she? the wonder of wonder possess of the power

to divine his inmost thought, to touch with magically heal finger

all the aching wound in his soul, to envelop he body and mind and

spirit in a network of a myriad fairy tendril? love she? God know he

do.



but she be a child—and a child can forget—at the bad retain a not

ungracious memory. but he be a man, on the verge of hideous villainy.

and he stand in his college room, surround by all that symbolize the

intellectual life that up to then have be the meaning of his existence,

and he look around.



“the whole lot will have to go to blaze,” say he.



and at that moment he cut the gordian knot.



his wife? she hate he: why, he could not tell; but she miss few

opportunity of show her rancour. he have strive desperately to win

her esteem, at the cost of much swallow pride. some month have pass

since the last pitiable reconciliation. . . . why have he marry she? it

have not be for lack of warning. perhaps the very traducing of she have

spur he on. she be so fair and fragile, so pathetic in her

widowhood. a clamour of the sense, a prompting of chivalry, and the

thing be do. and she, widow of a phlegmatic don of Trinity, live in

Cambridge, be perhaps carry away by the glamour surround the

come man in that tiny, academic world.



“I wish you be dead,” be the last word he have hear her utter. he

snap his finger. she could have her desire.



Baltazar pack his bag with necessary, tell his gyp that business

call he to London for some day, and leave Cambridge forever. a month

afterwards he be on his way, under an assumed name, to China.



the act of a fool perhaps. but have not one who know call he the Fool

of Genius? anyhow he have the courage and the wit to cut his life off

clean. the life of John Baltazar of Cambridge and that of James Burden

who, having land at Shanghai, spend so many adventurous year in the

heart of China, might have be live by two individual who have never

hear of each other. that disappearance from England be the first

start, the consequence of the first violent fit. the first that

matter.



but there have be other. to one, his mind go back even as he ask

himself whether his confession to Quong Ho have be the proceeding of an

idiot. it have to do with the selfsame subject of that confession. the

period go back to his last undergraduate term, when he be as certain

of be Senior Wrangler as a Cardinal of be the good theologian in a

scratch company of parish priest. carry on to the beginning of term

an end of vacation revel, Baltazar take to evil course. the slander

which, report to young Godfrey Baltazar, Marcelle Baring have so

vehemently deny, have its basis in truth. he have discover alcohol,

and for a time plunge, with his whole-souled fervour, into his

discovery. then, one Spooner, the next in the Tripos run, a man

live entirely on his scholarship, a mild and pallid man of no

physical value whom the lusty Baltazar, after the way of vivid and

immature young man, despise, have the grand audacity to call on he and

expostulate with he on his excess. Baltazar listen breathless. the

fellow ought to be go round with a show of freak. he tell he so.

Spooner wave aside the proposition and go on with his main argument.



“you have every right to be senior. there’s not one of we in it with

you. but if you go on play the fool like this, anything may happen.”



“that’s all to your personal advantage, my dear good missionary,” say

Baltazar.



“you don’t seem to understand why I’ve come here,” reply Spooner. “I

don’t want to be senior just because a man who’s infinitely well than

I be a drunken sot.”



and they talk and bandy word a little, and then Baltazar see

himself face to face with an exquisite soul. he grip the lean

shoulder of the undeveloped, spectacled young man with his big hand.



“I swear to God,” say he, “that I’ll not touch a drop of alcohol for

the next five year.”



but he also swear to himself an oath of which Spooner be ignorant. he

swear that Spooner should be senior. and he keep both vow. in the last

day’s Problem Paper he deliberately sacrifice himself. as a matter of

fact he just overdo it, for, to the mystification of all concerned in

the Tripos, he be place third. but Spooner have the coveted

distinction. the Tripos over, everything fall before Baltazar, and he

be acknowledge the supreme mathematician of his year, and, in the

course of time, the great of his generation.



                 *        *        *        *        *



the difficulty, owe to its episodical character, of present the

early career of Baltazar, thus find illustration. one might go back to

schoolboy day and point to lapse from grace, follow by similar swift

and ruthless decision. to catalogue they all would require the patient

tediousness of formal biography. apart from such a process, his life up

to his flight into the moorland wilderness can well be picture by a

series of flash.



a sudden disgust with China and an overwhelming nostalgia for the

sweeter political life of England drive he home after eighteen year.

the great part of the time he have spend in the impenetrable heart of

the vast country, speak many dialect as well as the classical Wen-Li

of the learn, an encyclopædia of erudition, saturate with intimate

knowledge of chinese custom and observance, a Chinaman in all but

physical appearance, dressing, living, act and accept universally

as a Chinaman, prosper as a Chinaman too in financial undertaking.

it be old China that he enter, a land stable in its peculiar

civilization which, in spite of many traditional oppression and

time-sanction cruelty, have its fascination and grace—the gift to a

Mandarin of a precious and much-covet ancient manuscript have purchase

the life of a boy, Li Quong Ho, condemn to elaborate death for a

venial offence, the transaction be carry out in an atmosphere of

high refinement, and scented tea serve and drunk with exquisite

punctilio. it be old China that he have learn to love, with its sense

of beauty, its reverence for learning, its profound ethical philosophy.

but it be a new China, convulse with new idea, bloodthirsty,

treacherous, unstable to madden point, that he have quit in his

sudden and determined way.



for eighteen year, in the interior of China, he have live remote from

european politic. he have sink himself in the lore, and identify

himself with the interest, of that ancient land. with no

correspondence, beyond the reach of newspaper, he all but forget the

existence of Europe. meet his fellow-countryman on the homeward

voyage, he shun they, partly through shyness, partly through distaste

for the brusqueness of their manner, the high pitch of their voice,

their colossal ignorance of the country with which they boast such

contemptuous familiarity, the narrowness of their outlook, the petty

materialism of their conversation. he hold himself aloof, long for

the real England at the end of the voyage.



in London, the lonely soul in the great city, he set himself to pick

up the thread of the life around he. he walk the familiar and

unwelcoming street, at first daze by the motor traction, then

bewilder by evidence of the luxury which eighteen year of decadence

have engender. he visit new palace of entertainment and come away

wonder. in fashionable supper-room he see the flower of the land

dance to what, as a scholar, he know to be west african sexual

rhythm. he could not understand. what be they do, or try to do?

he would sit lonely at a table, a formally order drink before he, at

one of these great public haunt, and try to get the key to the mystery.

the decay of manner offend he. he discount the fact that he have

live so many intense year in the land of sacred ceremonial; he wipe

that out of his mind, and recall the standard of his own youth. the

exiguity of feminine apparel shock his unaccustomed eye; in many

case nothing from waist up but a sort of low palisade, scarcely

conceal the bust. be he not mistaken? be this not rather the scum

than the flower of modern England? but at neighbouring table he have

overheard attention be direct to bearer of proud and historic

name. then he ask himself the question: have he frequent such place

eighteen year ago? have they not be outside the sphere of his narrow

academic life? he desire to judge justly. when do he leave England? in

1896. and his bachelor day, with their joyous London jaunt, have end

in 1894. there be no such social life then: if there have be, he would

have hear of it. in the afternoon, too, these young man and maiden

dance their weird dance.



outside, the land be a-clamour with the doing of a sterner sisterhood.

Processions, mass meeting, virago rioting, picture slashing,

incendiarism, bomb, form the feature of their astounding crusade.

the newspaper, beyond the recounting of fact, with vivid description

of sensational scene, give he little information as to the philosophy

of the movement. politically the country seem to be in a state of

chaotic turmoil. person hold high office be publicly accuse of

corrupt financial practice. Parliament wrangle fiercely with the Army

over an _opéra bouffe_ condition of irish affair. beneath all this

labour utter volcanic threatening. subversive idea, new to he, such

as syndicalism, be in the air. unintelligible criticism of picture

exhibition urge his curious step to the indicate gallery, where he

come upon canvas that make his brain reel. a new Rip Van Winkle, he

have awaken to a mad world, a world even more perilously unstable than

the China which he have leave.



the solitary scholar find himself disastrously out of sympathy with it

all. he have plan to give himself a month’s holiday in London before

settle down, in some quiet and comfortable suburb, to the many year’

work that lie before he on the material he have bring from China. he

have form no intention whatever of cut himself off from communion

with his fellow-man. indeed, he mean, as soon as he could rid himself

of the complication of his assumed name, to proclaim himself

unobtrusively to the world as John Baltazar. before come finally to

this decision, however, he must learn what have become of his wife, as he

have no desire to play the disconcert part of a tactless Enoch Arden.

his first step on arrive at London have be to institute, through a

firm of solicitor, discreet enquiry. he learn that his wife have

be dead for thirteen year. he be at liberty to become John Baltazar

again as soon as he like. but in London, as James Burden, he stay at

the Savoy Hotel, a bewildered and disillusioned spectator of the modern

world.



how do the catastrophe happen? think over it, as he often think

with shiver of disgust, in his moorland retreat, he could scarcely give

an answer. only once, since his interview with the audacious Spooner,

have he give way to an overmaster impulse—and that be on his

journey out to Shanghai. Anti-climax, in the shape of sudden storm and

sea-sickness, cure he, and he vow total abstinence all the time he

should be in China; and he keep his vow. perhaps, here in London,

unaccustomed idleness and his disgust-fill loneliness drive he

gradually and insensibly to the consolation of alcohol. the odd drink

during the day increase in number. he view a rosy London after a

quart of old Burgundy at dinner. to sit in a crowded cosmopolitan café

become his evening amusement, and the continuous consumption of brandy

and soda aid indulgent observation. he have give himself his month’s

holiday, and he mean to have it, no matter how joyless and

unsympathetic be the holiday atmosphere. now and then, in these popular

resort he pick casual acquaintanceship with a neighbour. he have the

gift of make his companion’s conversation intelligent and interesting.

on these occasion he drink less.



but one solitary night intoxication for the first time overcome he. he

realize it with a feeling of anger. the light be just be lower.

he order a double liqueur brandy, in the crazy assurance that it would

pull he together. of what happen afterwards he have little memory. in

the crowded street someone lay hold of he and, resentful of attack, he

turn and smite his supporter. to complete the outrage, a policeman

handle he roughly, a proceeding which he also violently resent. then

a whirl of light and darkness and light again, and strange face and

once more darkness absolute and final, until he awake and find himself

sober and shiver in a police cell. a few hour afterwards, James

Burden, of no occupation, live at the Savoy Hotel, be fine forty

shilling or a month for be drunk and disorderly in Leicester Square.



if it have be a magnificent folly, a royal debauch, a voluptuous orgy

of rose and wine and laughter and song and the pulsate lustiness of

life, the _dulce periculum_ of the follower of the Lenæan one brow-bind

with green vine-leave, he might have hold himself in some measure

excuse. he have make no vow, he have no reason, to spurn the joyousness

of existence. he be a man of race blood, with claim and right to the

gladness of physical thing. but this sordid, solitary bout with its end

of vulgarity and degradation, fill he with a horror almost madden

in its fierceness. his soul shrivel at the ghastly humiliation. that

it should come upon he; he, John Baltazar, with half a century of

clean life behind he; he, John Baltazar, the man who have compel

high honour for intellect and character from his childhood day, at a

Public School, at the University, as an unknown and prejudice-surround

foreigner in the strange of alien land; that it should come upon he

seem like a phantasma or a hideous dream.



and then it fall that he once more cut the gordian knot. he would fly

from a world in which he have prove himself not fit to live cleanly,

with all the less reluctance because he have find it incomprehensible

and unattractive. and sit dishevel on the bed, he inform Quong

Ho of his decision. as soon as he have cleanse himself from the soil of

the awful night, he leave the Savoy and the dishonour name of James

Burden for ever, and take room at another hotel for the night as John

Baltazar. the next day he throw himself vehemently into the quest of a

hermitage. he remember a desolate waste of moorland through which on a

walk tour he have ramble in his undergraduate day.



“it may be, Quong Ho,” say he, “that it be build over with picture

palace and swarm with tango-dancer. any conceivable happen to

England during the last twenty year be possible. but we’ll go and see.”



“I be unacquainted, sir,” reply Quong Ho, “with the dancer you

mention; but I have visit picture palace during the fortnight we have

spend in your wonderful country, and, rightly exercise, the

cinematograph strike I as be the most marvellous vehicle for the

propaganda of civilization that the world have see.”



“Quong Ho,” say Baltazar, “it be not in our contract to care one little

tuppenny damn for the propaganda of civilization. you’re not go to

waste your time at one of those futile and ill-conceive, although

ingenious, entertainment for the next three year. if the particular

region I have in view be not satisfactory, we shall find another.”



presently he add, in a tone of compunction—he be dress while

Quong Ho pack:



“I’m sorry I’ve have to cut short the time I intend you to have in

London. I badly want you to have some general idea of it.”



“Sir,” reply Quong Ho, “without wish to boast, I have grasp

London. I could find my way blindfold from here to the Tower, the

House of Parliaments, the North End Road, Fulham, and that imperishable

objective record of your honourable nation’s history, the museum of

Madame Tussaud.”



“all the point you have mention, Quong Ho,” say Baltazar, “be of

undoubted value—except the North End Road, Fulham. what the devil could

you find of interest in that drab region of nowhere?”



Quong Ho’s usually smile and mobile face become an expressionless

mask.



“it mark the end of my peregrination in that direction,” he reply.



“it strike I,” say Baltazar, “that it’s time you peregrinate to a

more God-sweep and intellectual atmosphere.”



three week afterwards they take up their residence at Spendale Farm.









                               CHAPTER V





BALTAZAR have live on the moor in peace and comfort for nearly a year

when he receive his first unsolicited communication from the outside

world, in the shape of a long, cheap envelope, head “on his Majesty’s

Service,” and contain Income Tax assessment form. for a moment he

wonder how the representative of his Majesty have manage to ferret

he out in his retreat.



“it’s a vile country,” say he to Quong Ho, who have hand he the

letter on return from his weekly visit to the town. “it’s a

pettifog, police-ride land, where a man, if he so choose, cann’t

bury himself decently. I’m sure the King be not aware of this

unwarranted interference with the liberty of one of the most

self-effacing of his subject.”



“my mind be in half,” reply Quong Ho, “to destroy the missive which I

conjecture would cause you annoyance.”



“it’s a good thing you don’t. the King be an amiable gentleman, but the

High Mandarins from whom this proceed be not to be trifle with.” he

glance through the paper. “it be well,” say he, with a sigh of

relief. “the High Mandarins around the Throne be as yet ignorant of my

whereabout; but if I refuse to obey this invitation, they would soon

learn it. it be a pestilential minor official in the vicinity who for

the sake of money—it’s his disgusting mode of livelihood—have violate

my solitude.”



“in the New China,” say Quong Ho, “we hope to do away with the

bureaucracy, which be a parasite on civilization.”



“you willn’t do it,” say Baltazar. “in the New Jerusalem—by which we

mean the Kingdom of Heaven—there be a Recording Angel, and you may bet

your boot he have get his staff of official who write minute and fill

up form all Eternity long.”



“Perfection,” remark Quong Ho, “be to be find neither in this world

nor the next, but only in that harmonious principle of the soul which be

term _li_ in the confucian philosophy.”



“Quong Ho,” say Baltazar in Chinese, “your wisdom befit rather the

honourable white beard of the teacher than the smooth-shaven chin of the

pupil of five-and-twenty.”



Quong Ho bow respectfully at the compliment and withdraw.



“confound the Income Tax!” say Baltazar, look through the paper. he

have completely forget his liability. the sudden reminder vex he.

of course he must pay; but his income be exclusively derive from

investment, all of which be tax at the source before the dividend

warrant be pay automatically into his account at his banker’, why

should he be worry? he resent the intrusion on his privacy.



a week later Quong Ho post the form in the ironically provide,

penny-save official envelope, and Baltazar dismiss the incident from

his mind.



when some time afterwards his assessment paper arrive, it cause he

some astonishment. he cast his memory back twenty year. in 1896 the

Income Tax, if he remember rightly, be inconsiderable, some sixpence

in the pound. now it be half a crown. he fill up the form, an easy

task, think less than ever of the social condition of Modern England;

such high direct taxation could only mean the desperate financial

strait of a decadent country. well, as far as he be concern, the

loss of one-eighth of his income do not matter. the initial expense of

his installation at Spendale Farm over, he scarcely spend a third of it.



the next disturbing document that find its way to Spendale Farm

contain a search series of question, head “National

registration.”



“I be cease to regard England as a fit place to live in,” say he,

with some petulance. “this be Mandarinism run riot.”



a few week afterwards he receive a neat little card fold in two, on

the outside of which be print a vile semblance of the Royal Coat of

arm and “National Registration Act, 1915,” and inside a certificate of

the Registration of (_a_) John Baltazar, (_b_) Philosophical

Investigator—for as such have he irritably describe himself—(_c_) of

Spendale Farm, Water-end. there be a space for the signature of Holder,

and below it in great capital “God save the king.” on the back be

direction as to change of address.



“God know what’s come over the country,” say he. “it appear that a

free-bear Englishman have get to carry about his police paper, as people

have to do in disgusting country like Germany and Russia. what about

you, Quong Ho? have you get a pretty little document like this?”



“I be register as an alien,” reply Quong Ho.



“it seem to I,” say Baltazar, “that when I use to gas to you about

our free british institution I be nothing but an ignorant liar.”



“by no mean, sir,” reply Quong Ho politely. “the keynote of the

modern world be change. what be true of material thing yesterday be a

lie to-day.”



“how do you discover that?”



“I assume the little town of Water-end to be but a microcosm of Great

Britain.”



“why,” laugh Baltazar, “what sign of change do you see there?”



Quong Ho remain for a moment silent, and his face assume its oriental

impassivity. if he report to his master the astounding event that

be take place, even at Water-End, whose quiet High Street be

a-bustle with newly fledge soldiery from the moorland camp three mile

on the further side, he would not only risk the dissolution of the

establishment, but would be guilty of filial disobedience, which be

impiety. and the European War, after all, how could it concern he, Li

Quong Ho? perhaps, too, his master, foresee the temp, particularly

desire to take shelter and hear nothing at all about it. he be

fortunate enough, however, to find a perfectly true reply to Baltazar’s

question. he smile in some relief; for an intellectual Chinaman,

train in the lofty morality of the chinese classic, do not

willingly lie.



“it be a woman and not a man who now deliver the letter in Water-end.”



Baltazar continue to laugh: “they’ll be drive the motor-car soon.”



“I’ve see they do it,” say Quong Ho.



“I’m not surprised,” say his master. “they be tend that way a year

ago. these new woman be out for the devirilization of man. perhaps by

this time they’re in Parliament, pass firework legislation and

play the devil with all our law and custom. you haven’t yet hear,

by any chance, whether the occupation of monthly nursing be confine

exclusively to the male sex?”



“the enactment, if such there be,” reply Quong Ho solemnly, “be not,

to my knowledge, in force in this remote locality.”



“let we thank the god, Quong Ho,” say Baltazar, “that we’re out of

this feminist hurly-burly. the little I see of the movement be

antipathetic to my philosophy of life. a society in which woman regard

the bearing of child as a physical accident of no account, and deny

the responsibility which such an event entail, must be doom to

decay, or, at the good, to bitter disillusionment. the more I hear of

contemporary England the less I like it. it seem to be woman-ridden;

curiously enough by two camp in apparent opposition, but in reality

wage joint warfare on man. the world have never yet behold such a sex

campaign. one section demand luxury beyond the dream of Byzantium at

its rottenest, and the other claim supreme political power.”



“it be well, sir,” say Quong Ho, “that you repudiate the imbecile

suggestion of the House Agent to the effect that you should employ a

woman housekeeper of mature age to superintend this establishment.”



“it be lucky for you, Quong Ho, that I do,” grin Baltazar. “she

would have make you sit up.”



Quong Ho, with clasped hand and lower head, respectfully assert

himself. “if I do not sit up sufficiently for your satisfaction, sir, it

be for you to reprimand I.”



“I only speak in jest, Quong Ho,” say Baltazar. “our western humour be

rather subtle.”



“I will make a note of it,” reply Quong Ho.



“by such notation and accumulation of detail one gather knowledge,”

say Baltazar. “by co-ordination one acquire wisdom. continue on this,

the only path of philosophy, and your old age will be bless. in the

meantime, please keep your observation of change at Water-end to

yourself.”



“obedience to your honourable command, my master,” reply Quong Ho, in

Chinese, “be the sacred duty of this entirely inconsiderable person. but

may one so inferior as myself humbly remind your illustrious greatness

that it be you who originally propound to I a question which I be

bind to answer.”



“the fact that I do so,” reply Baltazar, “you may note as an instance

of the human fallibility of the sublime mind. fear not but that I

will profit by your lesson.”



he wave a dismiss hand. Quong Ho bow with the perfect ceremonial

of pupil take leave of master and retire. Baltazar throw himself into

his arm-chair and laugh aloud.



“you’re a joy, Quong Ho. a perfect joy. a museum speciman of a joy.”



so while Baltazar delight in the unhumorous literalness of the

Chinaman, it never occur to he that he be the dupe of the

unhumorous literalness of the Chinaman’s fidelity; that while he be

inveigh against speculative phenomenon of an ill-understand movement,

the trumpet of war have transform that movement into an apotheosis of

feminine effort of which Quong Ho, keenly intellectual, be perfectly

well aware; and that it be only by the pious grace of his pupil and

servant that he live a day in his fool’s paradise.



when Quong Ho, a week afterwards, bring he his meagre mail, he

angrily crush in his fist and throw aside the enclosure of the first

envelope which he have open.



“I’m hang if this ben’t a begging circular! it’s infernal impudence!

it’s an intolerable outrage on one’s personal liberty. here, Quong

Ho!”—he sweep the remainder of the mail into the Chinaman’s hand.

“don’t let I be worried with any more letter. I’ve come down here to

be quiet and not to be badger. if there be bill to pay, make out the

cheque and I’ll sign they. if there be circular, throw they away.

about anything else use your discretion.”



“I will exactly execute your order,” reply Quong Ho.



thus Baltazar finally sever relation between himself and the outside

world. Quong Ho act the perfect private Secretary. the only letter

present to his master for perusal be rare business communication

from bookseller instruct to purchase some out-of-the-way and possibly

expensive book. circular letter, contain appeal for subscription,

which pour in, as soon as Baltazar’s name eventually find its way on

the address-list of the neighbourhood, Quong Ho conscientiously

destroy. use his discretion, he withhold letter from the Bank

invite investment in War Loans. such, in his opinion, be further

intrusion on the sacred privacy of his master. and thus the week and

month pass by; and Quong Ho, in touch with even such an outpost of

civilization as the tiny moorland town and bring to that contact the

most highly train incuriosity, could not avoid gather the current

tiding of the vast world conflict; but, faithful to his command, he

say never a word to Baltazar, give never a hint of the stupendous

convulsion in which the world be involve. and while his master, serene

doctrinaire, discourse on the political science of the ninety, now

be blow to smithereen by german gun, he maintain the reverential

attitude of the disciple, drink in as gospel truth the wisdom of his

inspire teacher.



one evening, when Baltazar have praise the clear solution of certain

problem which he have set in Differential Equations, and prophesy a

glorious career for the most brilliant mathematician China have ever

produce, Quong Ho, after gratefully acknowledge the encomium, say:



“if you will forgive my indiscretion, I should like to ask a question.

why be it, sir, that you, who take such great interest in the

future—for example, my inconsiderable and negligible prospect, and the

benefit that will accrue to humanity on the publication of the

thought-shake result of your own profound researches,—should be so

indifferent to the present condition of the world?”



“for the simple reason, my good fellow,” reply Baltazar, “that, from

what I have observe, the present condition of mankind—from China to

Peru, as your newly find friend Dr. Johnson say—be putrescent. the

good way in which we can serve mankind be to do what we’re do now—to

provide for the intellectual development of the future generation.”



“the proposition be unanswerable,” say Quong Ho. “but suppose, sir, for

the sake of argument, that a philosophic observation of the civilized

world as it be should result in the conclusion that, in the english

idiom, it be proceed fast to the devil—what be the duty of the man

of high morality?”



“to let it go slap-dash,” say Baltazar. “the fast and surer, the

well. for then the soon will the eternal rhythm, the eternal

principle of balance, assert itself. when a society be rush down to

gadarene suicide——”



“I beg your pardon, sir,” interrupt the alert Quong Ho. “Gad—I do not

understand the word.”



“read the Gospel accord to St. Mark to-morrow. you’ve hear of St.

Mark?”



“you might as well ask I, sir, if I have hear of Confucius or Homer, or

the immortal todhunter of my childhood.”



Baltazar rub his brown thatch and turn his luminous grey eye on

his disciple.



“the immensity of your purview, Quong Ho, be only equal by your

lightning perception of landmark. anyhow, read St. Mark over again, and

tell I your opinion of the swine of Gadara. for the moment, I’d have

you know that you’ve interrupt my argument. I be say that if

everything’s go to the devil—that’s the correct idiom—not

proceed to devil——”



“may I make a note of it?” say Quong Ho, scribble the phrase across

his mathematical manuscript.



Baltazar rise from his chair by the long deal table and relit his pipe

over the chimney of a lamp.



“you’ve put I out. what the blaze be we talk about?”



“the present world condition,” reply Quong Ho.



“then I assert,” say Baltazar, “that the present state of the world be

rotten. it’s no place for intellectual reformer like you and I. what

be the word of Confucius know to every schoolboy? ‘_with sincerity

and truth unite a desire for self-culture. Lay down your life rather

than quit the path of virtue. enter not a state which be totter to

its fall. when Law obtain in the Empire let yourself be see: when

lawlessness reign, retire into obscurity._’”



“but supposing,” persist Quong Ho, “the state of the devil-drive

world be of vital interest?”



“it can be of vital interest only to those hurtle down to destruction.

to we, who have retire into the obscure aloofness recommend by the

great philosopher, it can be of no possible concern.”



“it be well,” say Quong Ho.



“I know it be,” remark Baltazar, with a yawn. “another night let we

have a slightly more intelligent conversation.”



Quong Ho retire, his conscience finally set at rest. after all, be not

his master right? what could he do of any use in the world rudely at

war? be he not serve the true interest of humanity by retire at

this juncture and devote the harvest of his great learning to a future

generation?



“soldier,” say Quong Ho the next day, look into the unspeculative

topaz eye of the goat which he have be milk, “be as numerous as

the sand of the desert, and politician as the mosquito in a swamp;

they be sweep away and the world miss they not; but philosopher be

rare, and the loss of one of they be a supreme world calamity.”



“Baa-a-a!” say the goat.



“I perceive that you too have wisdom,” say Quong Ho. “you appreciate

the privilege of live under the same roof as the illustrious

Baltazar.”



he burst into an unaccustomed laugh. conversation with a goat appeal

to his prim sense of humour. but all the same, he express his own

deeply-root conviction. to the keen-brain young Chinaman, Baltazar

appear as a man of stupendous intellectual force. his knowledge of the

abstract science of the western world would have command his respect;

but his vast chinese erudition, acknowledge with admiration by

Mandarins and scholar and other Great Ones of China, give Quong Ho

cause for a veneration reach almost to idolatry.



also Baltazar, for all his patriarchal year, earn his pupil’s respect

as a man of marvellous muscle and endurance. during the winter, when the

inclemency of the weather forbid agricultural pursuit—and on that

moorland waste the weather abandon itself to every capricious devildom

within meteorological possibility—Baltazar, having order a set of

glove from London, give box lesson to his disciple. at first Quong

Ho be shocked. how could so contemptible a person as he ever make a

pretence of smite the highly honourable face of his master? Baltazar

bid he try. he would give he an hour’s extra private tuition for

every hit. and Quong Ho, encourage by so splendid a prize, try, at

first diffidently, then earnestly, then zealously, then desperately,

then bald-headedly, but never a wild blow could pass the easy guard of

his smile master.



“you see, Quong Ho, it’s a science,” say Baltazar. “now I’m go to

hit you.” and he feint and strike out with his left and send his

disciple swinge across the room. “it be also a game,” he add,

hold up his hand, “because what I have just do do not hurt you in

the least.”



Quong Ho rub his jaw. “it be like the kiss of a butterfly,” say he.



“here endeth the First Lesson,” say Baltazar. “the english etiquette

now require that we should shake hand.”



when they have go through the formality Baltazar continue:



“you of all non-english people oughtn’t to be astonish. do not the

same ceremony exist in your country over two thousand year ago? be it

not refer to in the Analects?”



“Sir,” say the breathless and perspire Quong Ho, “I have unworthily

forget.”



“do not the Master say: ‘_the true gentleman be never contentious. if a

spirit of rivalry be anywhere unavoidable, it be at a shooting-match.

yet even here he courteously salute his opponent before take up his

position_’—we ought to have shake hand before start, but we’ll do

it next time—‘_and again when, having lose, he retire to drink the

forfeit-cup_’—your forfeit-cup be the loss of the extra hour of

tuition. ‘_so that even when compete, he remain a true gentleman._’”



“I remember now,” say Quong Ho.



“I’m glad you do,” reply Baltazar. “that be the lofty spirit in which

we shall continue this exceedingly health-give science and pastime.”



and they continue. the young Chinaman, lithe, hard, physically perfect,

little more than half the age of his tutor, devote himself, with his

chinese assiduity, to the mastery of the fascinating art, and succeed

eventually in give Baltazar most interesting encounter; he realize

that fierce blow plant on venerable feature be take, nay

applaud, in the spirit of the confucian gentleman; he also accept in

the same gentlemanly way the hammering that he invariably receive. it

be after some month of this training, when he be able to discount

merely superior science, that he bow down before Baltazar not only as

before an intellect, but as before a marvellous physical man.



there come a truce, however—the follow winter—when Baltazar, wise

in his elderly generation, foresee the inevitable supremacy of youth,

and order new toy from London—foil, mask and fencing jacket. the

glove moulder in a break-down potting-shed, and Quong Ho again

start, as a tyro, to learn a new athletic accomplishment. thus in his

disciple’s sound body Baltazar contrive to maintain a sound and humble

mind. he know that he be hold in deep respect by Quong Ho. but it never

occur to his careless mind that Quong Ho regard he as a kind of

god. he accept the homage as a matter of course.



in these idyllic condition John Baltazar account himself serenely

happy. his scholarly solitude be undisturbe by the windy way of man

or the windy way of moorland nature. the former spend themselves before

reach he; at the latter he snap his finger. what to he be the

season’ difference? so absorb be he in his work, so circumscribe in

his walled enclosure beyond which he seldom set foot, that he barely

even notice the hourly change on the sensitive face of the moor. and

season follow season, and the pile of manuscript, exquisitely

correct for the printer, grow in height, and Quong Ho assimilate

Higher Mathematics as though it be rice; and everything be for the

good in the good of all possible little intellectual world.









                               CHAPTER VI





SUCH, as far as a few stroke can picture he, be John Baltazar, at the

time when his unsuspected son lie footless in the convalescent home and

discuss with Marcelle bare the mystery of his existence. a man of

many failing, many intolerance, of some ruthlessness. a man both

sensitive and hard; both bold and shrink; with the traditional habit

of the ostrich and the heart of a lion. a man apparently give to

extravagance of caprice; and yet remain always constant to himself,

preserve also throughout his strange career a perfect unity of

character. perhaps, regard he from another point of view, his

detractor may say that he love to play to himself as audience and,

far, put that audience in the gallery. why not? it be in the essence

of human consciousness that a man must, in some measure, be an actor to

himself. the degree depend on the human equation. duma _fil_ once

say of his immortal semi-mulatto father: “he be quite capable of

get up behind his own carriage, in order to persuade people that he

keep a black footman.” a savage epigram. but it would have be a

deep truth if he have say that the wonder of a man who be his father,

be capable of do it, in order to persuade himself that he keep a

black footman. the more we limit the audience to the man himself, the

more we love he. the more human do the vivid creature appear to we.

if Baltazar play to that audience of one, he have many illustrious

colleague. if again his method be melodramatic, it at least have

breadth. it deal with big issue in a broad and simple way. . . .



“that’s what I love about the three great system of chinese ethic,” he

various proposition or you, don’t. there be no _homoousian_ and

_homoiousian_ conflict, and suchlike rubbish, that have tear western

thought to ribbon for over a thousand year. in China you go straight

to the heart of truth. all the subtlety lie, Quong Ho, in the correct

interpretation of your appalling but fascinating script.”



this be a rough profession of faith, almost an analysis of character.

the intellect of the mathematician delight in the process of arrive

at exactness of statement, but at the same time that statement’s

philosophic simplicity appeal to a nature fundamentally simple.



he abhor complication. that be his weakness. he claim,

unphilosophically, the absolute. hence the abandonment of his academical

mortal man have ever undertake. who could tell whither those adventure

could lead? pure mathematic have demonstrate the existence of the

the next world might be four-dimensional and the spirit of the dead who

“_the angry terror of compassionate Heaven extend through this low

he laugh out loud, shut the book and return it to the shelf.



“‘I be greatly pain’! oh, my Lord!”

Brutus.”



the dog, hear his name, rest his long chin against his master’s

Quong Ho present the dish, and Baltazar and Brutus get their desert.



presently Quong Ho bring in lamb cutlet with fresh pea from the

“Quong Ho,” say Baltazar, “you’re a wonder. be there anything you cann’t

when Quong Ho appear, book and paper as usual under his arm,

they talk on, develop the idea of wedding of the material and the

Quong Ho, who have rise when his master rise, say:

“I want to eradicate from my mind the soul-destroy association of

then Baltazar laugh aloud and clap the young Chinaman on the

he look fondly around the long, low-ceilinge room, brilliantly

“what a Heaven-send thing be Peace,” say Baltazar.

air around, above they. John Baltazar put his hand to a bewildered head.

what unheard-of convulsion of nature be this? then suddenly he have a

second’s consciousness of burst flame and overwhelming crash, and the

blackness of death submerge his sense.









                              CHAPTER VII





when he recover consciousness it be but to awake to an

incomprehensible dream condition. of his whereabouts he have no notion.

an attempt to move cause he such hideous pain in his head as almost to

render he again unconscious. his limb, too, seem under the control

of dream paralysis. he lie for a while co-ordinate his faculty,

until he arrive at the definite conviction that he be awake. his eye

rest on ashlar of granite which, as he lie on his left side,

he feel sick and faint. by an effort of will he move a leg. the

movement reveal unaccustomed stiffness of limb: it also reawaken the

torture of his head. again he stay motionless. yes, it be daylight.

it be sunlight; some twenty foot far down the wall cast a shadow.

presently over his recover sense steal an abominable stench. he

sniff, jerk his head to its intolerable agony. cautiously he lift

his right hand to the seat of pain. his finger dabble in something

like thick glue. bring they down before his eye, he see they be

“let we concentrate on this: nothing else for the moment matter.” he

with the same abominable stench.



as soon as he could gather sufficient physical energy he rise to a

find himself begrime by it. he sit forward, stare, and, secure of

terror of Hell opening—and nothingness. yes, he remember. it be

dense mist when they go out. now it be clear, beautifully clear. the

sun be shine; but it be low on the horizon; so it must be early

morning.



what could have happen? a thunderstorm? the place strike by lightning?

he grip his temple. he have never hear of a thunderstorm in a dense

fog. besides, thunder never occur in the long, continuous, rhythmical

acceleration of volume of sound. yet what else but thunder and lightning

could account for the blasted homestead that reek before his eye?



he look around. the stone enclosure be strew with unspeakable

his brow the handkerchief which he mechanically draw out, he see, close

his pocket. the dog seem to have be kill outright by a great piece

mind grow quite clear. the unknown convulsion have deal not only

destruction but death. where be Quong Ho?
