proverbial longevity of don? who now be master of his college? when he

leave, Fordyce be get a bit elderly. why, of course, by now, if

alive, he would be over ninety. Fordyce must have be gather long ago

to his father. who could have succeed he? why haven’t he look it up

in a book of reference? it seem stupid to return to his own college

without know the name of the master. who be the prominent people?

Westgrove, the senior tutor; Barrett, senior dean; Withington, junior

dean; Raymond, bursar; Smith, Hartwell, Grayson, Mostyn—man more or

less of his own standing; sheepshank, the famous mathematical coach

upon whose shoulder have fall the mantle of the immortal Routh (maker

of senior wrangler), and his own private tutor and friend. there would

be somebody there out of all that lot, at any rate. he feel more

hopeful.



a grizzle porter throw his suit-case into a hansom cab, a welcome

survival of his youth, and in answer to his query whether the “Blue

Boar” be still in existence, stare at he as though he have question

the stability of the great court of Trinity or Matthews, the Grocers.



“the ‘Blue Boar,’ sir? why, of course, sir.”



so to that ancient hostelry Baltazar drive down Trumpington Street. it

seem all new and perky until he come to the great landmark, the

Fitzwilliam Museum. then in a flash he recapture his Cambridge:

peterhouse on his left; Pembroke on his right; the three-sided, low,

bricke court of St. Catherine’s face the dignified stone front and

gateway of Corpus; then the amazing grandeur of King’s College

Chapel—he crane his head out and drink in its calm loveliness; then

the Senate House; on the right the shop of the King’s Parade, just as

they use to be; then Caius, and the cab draw up at the “Blue Boar.”



he secure a room and go out again to fill his lung with the

atmosphere of the beloved place, his soul with its beauty and its

meaning. he wander, at first like a man distraught, his eye far above

the pavement, wrapt in the familiar glory of stone and brick; the

majesty of Trinity, the twin-tower, blazon gateway of St. John’s,

the venerable round church of the Holy Sepulchre. . . . he walk on

past Sidney, Christ’s, Emmanuel; turn up Downing Street. at the sight

of the vast pile of modern science building, he come down to earthly

thing. thenceforward he become aware of something new and strange and

alien to the academic spirit that once spread its brood wing over

the town. the quiet street be fill with soldiery. Khaki, khaki, on

road and pavement; khaki, khaki, in college court. there seem to be

regiment of rank and file. officer, gaitere and spur, clank

along as in a garrison city. much youth, whose status he could not

determine, wear a white band round its cap, laugh and jest,

undergraduate-like, on its way. he wander through the river-nest of

college, Queen’s, Clare, Trinity Hall, through court and gateway, and

it be the same story of military occupation. a bevy of nurse flit

about the court of King’s. a group of man in hospital blue lounge over

the balustrade of Clare Bridge.



it be a wondrous metamorphosis. almost the only young man in civilian

attire be a few indian student. he come across they carry

notebook under their arm, on their return from morning lecture.

lecture, then, be still go on. college authority be still in

residence; he have, in fact, pass many unmistakable don. but don and

Indians seem but the relic of a past civilization. in a spasm of

amazement he realize that the University, as he have conceive it, a

seat of learning, no long exist. the three thousand young man, the

average undergraduate population, who afford the University its reason

of be, be fight for their country or be train in the art

of war. yet the college through which he pass seem to be alive. no

sign anywhere of desolation or decay. Pembroke and Emmanuel have the

appearance of barrack. he stride hither and thither, in his impetuous

way, his mind exercise with the wonder of it all; see Midsummer Common

fill with troop at drill, find himself on the river. the tow-path

be overgrow with grass. War everywhere. the very boat-house be

incorporate into the military system. on the familiar front of his own

college boat-house be nail an inscription. such and such a regiment.

officer’ mess.



the University be at war. not for the first time in its glorious

history. troop have garrison his college in the Civil Wars. it have

melt down its plate for Charles the First. if it have possess a

boat-house it would have give it loyally to the king. yet that be

between two and three hundred year ago. Baltazar have the modern and not

the archæological instinct. condition be different in those day. but

now, in the second decade of the twentieth century, to be confront

with his remote, innocent college boat-house thus draw, a vital though

tiny unit, into the war, spur his imagination to a new

comprehension of the world-convulsion to which he have be but recently

awaken. if the war could reach and grip a pretty balconied shed on the

River Cam, in what other infinite ramification through the whole of the

national life do its tentacle not extend? as he retrace his step to

the town, the bombing of Spendale Farm and the commandeering of his

college boat-house appeal to he as the two most significant fact of

the war.



                 *        *        *        *        *



he stand in the gateway under the groin roof by the porter’s lodge of

his own college. the porter on duty, a young, consumptive-look man,

appear at the door. Baltazar say:



“I be an old member of the college, and I’ve be abroad for many year.

I wonder if there’s anybody in residence whom I use to know.”



“it depend upon who you want to see, sir.”



Baltazar search the young man’s face. “First”—he snap finger and

thumb—“yes, first, where’s westmacott?”



“my father, sir? he’s feel his age, and have a bit of a holiday.

do you know he, sir?”



“of course I do. he be senior porter when I be an undergraduate. he

must be about a hundred and ten.”



“no, sir, only seventy-five,” smile the young man.



“who’s master now?”



“Dr. Barrett, sir.”



“be he up?”



“not for the moment, sir.”



“what about Mr. Westgrove?”



“Westgrove? oh yes, sir. he die a long time ago. when I be a boy,

sir.”



“well, who be there in residence?”



the young Westmacott rattle off a string of unfamiliar name.



“I’m talk of twenty year ago,” say Baltazar. “what about Mr.

Raymond?”



“he’s Professor of Economics at—at one of those new sort of

university, sir.”



the Cambridge-train servitor’s tone express both regret at Mr.

Raymond’s decline and scorn of the new sort of university.



“Mr. Sheepshanks——?”



“Dr. Sheepshanks now, sir. _Honoris causa._ just before the war.”



“well, Dr. Sheepshanks then,” say Baltazar, rather impatiently.



“oh, he’s always here, sir. he’s senior tutor.”



“be he in?”



“I haven’t see he go out to-day. I’m pretty sure he’s in, sir. letter

E, New Court.”



“thank,” say Baltazar, and go in search of sheepshank, through the

familiar court.



when he stand at the doorway of Letter E and read the name,

white-lettered on black, “Dr. Sheepshanks,” he remember that here

sheepshank have live thirty year ago. probably the same room. on the

second floor. he mount the wind wooden stair. yes: above the

unsported oak (the infallible porter be right) the name of Dr.

Sheepshanks be inscribe. he pause for an instant before knock at

the inner door, because all his youth come surge back on he. he see

himself a freshman, tap with nervous knuckle at the almost sacred

portal of the famous coach, the fount of all mathematical science, the

legendary being who have the power to make senior wrangler at will. he

see himself the third year man, rap confidently, secure in the

knowledge that sheepshank have stake his reputation on his triumph. he

see himself smite the door defiantly, after the list have be

publish . . . “Spooner, Jenkins, Baltazar . . .” Spooner have read with

Roberts of Trinity; but Jenkins have be a Sheepshanks man. . . . he see

himself, many and many a time afterwards, when he have step into his

universally acknowledge own, thump it with friendly familiarity.

that heavy, black oak door, invitingly open, hold the secret of his

vivid youth.



at last he knock, but the knock—so it seem—be devoid of

character. a voice—the same sharp, nasal voice—it send he back again

to freshman’s day—cry:



“come in.”



he open the door, stand on the threshold. the back of sheepshank,

work at his desk by the great window look over the master’s

garden, meet his eye, across the large library table that occupy the

centre of the room. it be the same old table—the table at which he have

sit with the superior first batch of pupil, during his undergraduate

day. how often then and in after day he have enter on that crack

“come in,” and see that lean back and bow head, and wait the few

second, as he be do now, for the owner to finish his sentence and

swing round in his chair—the same old swivel-chair. after the same

second or two, Sheepshanks turn round and, as in one movement, rise to

his foot. he be a small, brown, wrinkle, clean-shaven man in the early

sixty, with eye mask by thick myopic lense, spectacle set in gold

rim. his hair short, but curly, gleam a dazzling white. it be a

shock of memory to Baltazar to realize that when he have last see it, it

be raven black.



“yes?” say sheepshank, enquiringly.



Baltazar stride past the library table with outstretched hand.



“don’t pretend you’ve never see I before, sheepshank.”



sheepshank make a step forward, peer through his glass, then

recoil and gasp:



“Baltazar!”



“you’ve hit it, my dear old friend. I’m not a ghost. I’m live flesh and

blood. I’m John Baltazar right enough.”



“God bless my soul!” say sheepshank. “we think you must be dead. do

sit down.”



Baltazar laugh as he turn to deposit hat and stick on a side-table;

then he come and clap both his hand on the elderly don’s lean

shoulder.



“you apostle of primness! ben’t you glad to see I?”



“of course I’m glad, my dear fellow. exceedingly glad. but your sudden

resurrection rather take one’s breath away.” he smile. “let we both

sit down, and you can tell I all about it.”









                               CHAPTER XI





if I don’t smoke, I’m afraid I cann’t talk,” say Baltazar.



sheepshank smile politely. “you remember my little weakness? but pray

smoke. I’ve got use to it of late year. time change, and we with

they.”



Baltazar fill and light his pipe.



“a couple of week ago,” say he, “I have all but complete two

epoch-mark mathematical treatise. I have get system and result you

good people here have never dream of. I have also stuff in the way of

chinese scholarship that would have be a revelation to the western

world. then german aircraft drop bomb on my house, a hermitage in

the middle of a moorland, and wipe out the labour of a lifetime. they

also nearly kill a young chinaman whom I regard as an extraordinary

mathematical genius and about whom I want to consult you. they also,

thereby, reveal to I a fact of which I be entirely unaware, namely,

that the war have be go on for a couple of year.”



he lean back in his chair and draw a few contented puff. his host

pass a hand over perplex brow and lean forward.



“I’m very sorry,” say he, in his precise, nasal voice, “to appear

stupid. but you have put forward half a dozen such amazing proposition

in one breath that I cann’t quite follow you.”



a smile gleam in Baltazar’s eye. “I think that would get you,” he

remark placidly. “but it’s an accurate presentment of my present

position.”



“no doubt, no doubt,” say sheepshank. “but you surely haven’t be

live a recluse on a moor for the last twenty year?”



“oh no,” reply Baltazar. “eighteen of they I spend in China. I go

out straight from here.”



“to China? dear I,” say sheepshank. “what an extraordinary place to

go to from Cambridge.”



“don’t anybody guess where I have vanish to?”



“not a soul, I assure you. your disappearance create a sensation. quite

a sensation. a painful one, because you be a man we could ill afford

to lose.”



“it’s good of you to say so. but it’s odd that no one seem to be

interested enough in I to reason out China. you all know I be keen on

Chinese.” he cast a swift glance around the bookshelf that line the

room, and shoot out an arm. “I shouldn’t be surprised if that’s my little

handbook—_Introduction to the Language, on a Scientific Basis_.”



sheepshank’ myopic vision follow Baltazar’s point finger.



“yes. it’s somewhere there. you haven’t change much from the creature

of flash that you use to be.”



“it happen to be the only yellow-back book on the shelf. to say

nothing of the purple dragon, which be grossly incorrect and unmeaning.

it jump to the eye. just as my go to China ought to have jump to

the eye of everybody.”



“I’m afraid it don’t. perhaps we be too much paralysed with dismay.”



“I often try to guess what you all think about it,” say Baltazar.

“a human being cann’t escape his little vanity. it be like be dead

and wonder what the dicken people be say about one.”



“we don’t know what to say,” reply sheepshank. “we have no precedent

on which to base any conclusion. we look for motive for flight and

we could find none. we seek for possible imperative objective, and

one so apparently uncompelling as China never occur to we. here

to-day, go to-morrow. you vanish, ‘like a snowflake on a river.’ to

see you now, after all these year, look scarcely a day old, be an

experience which I must confess be bewilder.”



“I suppose you think I mad or a fugitive from justice, or one drive

by the Furies.”



“we don’t know what to think, and that’s the truth of it,” reply

sheepshank.



“well, call it the last. I ben’t very old and harden. perhaps I

mistake Mrs. Grundy with an upraised umbrella for one of the lady who

play the devil with Orestes and Company. I have quite decent reason

then for clear out. whether I be wise or not be another matter.

anyhow I clear, sink my identity and go out to China. after eighteen

year I come back. the rest I’ve tell you in a sort of pemmican form.”



“I don’t deny,” say sheepshank, “that I be still somewhat confused.”



“all right,” say Baltazar. “you sit there, and I’ll tell you what I

can. anyhow, I’ll try to explain why I’m here. I’ll begin from the day I

sail for China.”



the primness of Edgar Sheepshanks,D.SC., relaxed, to some extent, during

Baltazar’s story. like Dominie Sampson’s “prodigious!” his “wonderful!

wonderful!” punctuate the interval. to he who have stick limpet-like

to the same academic wall, Baltazar appear a veritable modern

Ulysses. he sigh, wish that he too have perform the scholarly

travel through that far land of Mystery, the Cathay of ancient time,

which be now the little well know interior of modern China; he

sigh, as he do when gallant youth return from high adventure in

that land of equal mystery, the Front. Baltazar be half through his

tale when there enter a venerable man-servant, sheepshank’s gyp for

innumerable year. at the sight of the guest he start back with the

drop jaw of one who see a ghost. “Mr. Baltazar!”



“Lord, it’s Punter!”



it be odd how name come back from the moss-grow recess of memory.

he shake hand with the old man.



“yes, it’s I. and you’re look just as young as ever. I recognize

you at once. and look here, Punter, if you want to do I a service, just

spread the news about Cambridge. if I’ve get to go through an Ancient

Mariner or Wandering Jew explanation every time I meet anyone, it’ll

eventually get on my nerve.”



“I’m sure every one will rejoice to have you back, sir,” say the gyp.



“Punter’s bring my lunch. I hope you’ll stay and share it with I,”

say sheepshank politely.



“delight,” say Baltazar, and the old man having retire, he go on

with his tale.



he continue it over lunch in the next room, a homelier chamber, where

sheepshank keep his choice book and his two or three good italian

picture and a few ivory and photograph of nephew and niece. it be

during the meal that he notice for the first time a lack of

effusiveness on the part of his host. not that he have expect the prim

sheepshank to throw his arm about he and dance with joy; but he have

hope for more genial sign of welcome. after all, he reflect, he have

let the college down very badly; possibly he be still unforgiven. well,

if that be so, he would have to earn forgiveness.



in his tale he have reach the first visit to London.



“I be out of my element, as you perceive,” say he, “and then something

happen which make I decide suddenly to go into seclusion for two or

three year. real seclusion. I don’t do thing by half. in some remote

spot where not a whisper of the outer world could ever reach I.”



“but what kind of thing could have happen to cause you to take such an

extraordinary step?” ask Sheepshanks.



Thought Baltazar: “if I tell he the real reason, he’ll turn into a

pillar of frozen don.” besides, he have not the faint intention of

open his soul to sheepshank, even though the latter should have

enact the part of the father of the Prodigal Son. he wave the

question aside.



“nothing of any importance. just one of the idiot trifle that always

seem to arise and deflect my course through life. the main point be that

I find the place I want, and go there with Quong Ho.”



Luncheon have be clear away and he have finish a couple of pipe

before he come to the end of his narrative.



“so now you see my position,” say he.



“I think I do,” reply sheepshank.



“my whole life-work have go—except that part of it which exist in the

cultivate brain of my remarkable young Chinaman. there seem to be no

place for I in London, where everybody’s fit into the war, where I’m

simply daze and unwanted. so I’ve come here—if only to find something

left of my old life to attach myself to.”



“I’m afraid there’s not very much to be do in Cambridge,” say

sheepshank. “it’s no long a university, but a military camp.”



“but at any rate,” say Baltazar, “I can find here a few human being I

know who might put I in the way of actual thing—help I on my

course.”



“that’s quite possible,” say sheepshank.



“I also have to see what can be do for Quong Ho. I want he to come up

next term. have the college ever have an undergraduate who have come up

with a knowledge of Elliptic Functions?”



“God bless my soul!” ejaculate sheepshank, in interested astonishment.



“he’s a wonder,” laugh Baltazar. “I ought to know, because I’ve teach

he daily for ten year. well, he’ll be on your list, if you’ll have

he. he’s a dear creature. manner like a Hidalgo. Mind cultivate in

the good of chinese and english literature. and speak English like his

favourite author, Dr. Johnson.”



sheepshank smile, a very pleasant smile, in which every wrinkle of his

dry brown face seem to have a part.



“how you keep your enthusiasm, Baltazar!”



“Quong Ho be worth they. you’ll see. as soon as he’s fit for it, I’ll

send he to you. you set he last June’s Tripos Papers—Part II, if you

like. I’ll bet you anything he’ll floor they. of course I’m

enthusiastic,” he say, after re-light his pipe, which have go out.

“I’ve no kith or kin in the world. I’ve adopt Quong Ho as my

intellectual son and heir.”



sheepshank rise, walk to the open window deliberately and look out.

presently he turn.



“it seem strange,” say he, “that you should adopt a Chinaman, when

your english son be give great promise of follow in your

footstep.”



Baltazar regard he in a puzzled way. then he laugh.



“my stepson. I’m afraid, my dear sheepshank, when I leave the mother I

leave her son. one of the defect of my quality be honesty. I may be

brutal, but I cann’t take a sentimental interest in the son of old Doon.”



“the man I’m talk about,” say sheepshank, in the precise clip,

nasal manner under which Baltazar remember many a delinquent and

uppish pupil to have wilt in the old day, “ben’t call Doon. his

name be Baltazar. he come up with a Minor Scholarship over the way”—he

wave a hand, indicate the grey wing of the neighbouring college

visible through the window—“and he be the most promising freshman of

his year.”



Baltazar rise too.



“I don’t know what on earth you’re talk about. I don’t suppose I’m

the only Baltazar leave in England. he can be no son of mine. it’s

idiotic. you ought to know.”



“I do know,” say sheepshank.



Baltazar’s eye flash in amazement and he make a stride towards he.

“what do you know? what be you suggest?”



“a child be bear here in Cambridge, three month after you leave we.”



something almost physical seem to hit Baltazar between the eye,

partially stun he. he feel his way to the near chair and sit

down.



“my God!” say he. “oh, my God!”



he remain for some time, his head on his hand, overwhelm by the

significance of the revelation. at last he spring suddenly to his foot.



“no wonder you haven’t forgive I,” he cry, with characteristic

directness. “to run away from a woman in such circumstance would be the

unforgivable sin. but I swear to God I never know. she give no hint, and

I see she only a few day before I leave. such a possibility never

enter my mind. have never enter it. I may be any kind of a sinner,

but not such a scoundrel as that. I leave she because we be miserable

together.—I do my good—now and then a brief reconciliation.—I

suppose she try too, in she way.—After the last, thing be bad

than ever. and then there be the life of someone else I couldn’t

sacrifice—a flower of a thing. I feel my wife would be glad to see the

last of I. so I flee like Christian from the Burning City. if I have

know that—well, that I be leave this responsibility behind I, I

should have face thing out. my God! man, you must believe I,” he

end passionately.



sheepshank through his thick gold spectacle meet Baltazar’s fierce gaze

for a few moment. then he hold out his hand: “I believe you, J. B., and

do so take a great load off my mind.”



“I’ve notice your avoidance of the old name,” say Baltazar. “it must

have be in pretty evil odour for the past twenty year or so.”



“you’re such an incalculable fellow,” say sheepshank, with a kind

smile. “the romance you so delicately suggest never occur to any of

we.”



“well, well,” say Baltazar, “all that be do and over long ago.

anyhow, I ben’t the heartless wretch Cambridge must have take I for.

I leave my rehabilitation in your hand. to I now the main, stare,

extraordinary fact be that I have a son. a son. I, who think I be

wander lonely as What’s-his-name’s cloud. I’ve get a son. a

mathematician. the same lunatic quirk of brain. if he be the village

idiot—it would be different.—You remember the ghastly story of Guy de

Maupassant? but not only my own flesh and blood, but my own flesh, blood

and intellect.” he pace about the room. “what kind of a fellow be he?

be he like I? have you see he?”



“yes; once. Crosby—you remember Crosby?” he wave a hand towards the

college visible through the window.



“yes, yes,” say Baltazar, impatiently.



“Crosby ask I to breakfast, one day, to meet he. the son of John

Baltazar, senior mathematical scholar of his year, be a curiosity. we

don’t tell the young man so. indeed, I suppose he wonder why such an

old fossil like myself be there.”



“never mind what he think of old fossil, my dear sheepshank. what

be he like?”



“like you. quite recognizable. but fair, and though sensible and

manly, less—if you will allow I to say so—less of a firebrand.”



“anyhow, a good straight chap. not merely low mathematical cunning

envelop in any kind of smug exterior?”



“he’s a son any father would be proud of,” say sheepshank.



“and where be he now?”



sheepshank make a vague gesture. “where be all the gallant youth of

England? over there, fight.”



“be you sure?”



“it would be small compliment to you, J. B., if I ben’t sure,” reply

sheepshank with a smile. “the only undergraduate leave in the

University be a few unhappy youngster reject from the army for

physical reason. the maim, halt and blind; also medical student

hurry through their course, and the usual contingent of indian

student who, not belong to the fight race of India, can find no

place in the army of Great Britain.”



“I don’t care about paralytic or doctor or Indians,” say Baltazar. “I

want to know about this son of mine.”



“Crosby would tell you. he’s up. I see he yesterday. of course, you

know he’s master now.”



“Crosby?” cry Baltazar, incredulously. “Crosby—that pragmatical owl,

master of——?”



“even as you be master of intolerance,” sheepshank interrupt.

“Crosby have develop into a very great man, and there’s not a head of

house in the University who be more beloved by his college. you’ll find

he in intimate touch with half a dozen generation of undergraduate.”



“I’m learn thing every minute,” say Baltazar. “so much for Crosby.

I’ll go along and see he. but the boy—I suppose he have get a Christian

name. what be it?”



“I forget—but I can easily find out.” sheepshank take _the Cambridge

University Calendar_ from a shelf. “but perhaps you’d like to look

through it yourself.”



Baltazar turn rapidly over the page, find the college he seek and

the name of Godfrey Baltazar in its list of scholar.



“Godfrey!” he exclaim. “that be my father’s name.” then after a

pause, as though speak to himself: “it be good of she. damned good

of she.”



he walk to the casement window which Sheepshanks have vacate and

lean his elbow on the sill, look out for a long time into a blur

of thing. sheepshank glance at his broad shoulder which seem bow

beneath an intolerable burden, and after a moment or two of hesitation

slip noiselessly from the room. presently Baltazar turn, start to

find himself alone, frown, then recognize a delicate instinct on the

part of his host, go back to the window and his whirl of thought and

emotion.



what a mess he have make of his life! what folly have be each one of

those flame decision that have mark his career! be he a coward? the

word sting. there be a difference between fly from temptation and

resist it. he remember the comparison he have just make between

himself and Christian fly from the Burning City, and suddenly see the

meanness and selfishness of Bunyan’s Hero—egotism as colossal as that

of St. Simeon Stylites on whom he have once airily lecture to Quong Ho.

what matter anything human, wife, child bear and the child within

the womb, so long as he save his own wretchedly unimportant soul? for

aught Christian care, all his family and his friend could go literally

to Hell, so long as he himself escape. a sorry figure. and just such a

sorry figure have cut John Baltazar. and, life be real and implacable,

he have not even succeed in save his paltry soul. he have lose it at

every step. his fine phrase to Quong Ho; his boast of altruistic

service to mankind? Sheer juggle with sacred thing. sheer egotism.

sheer vanity.



what a mess he have make of his life! what folly have be his cowardly

flight! if he have know, he would have remain. yes. a salve to

conscience. but the conscience of brave man need no salve.



he have fool away his life in a country that have no need of he, from

which he have derive no measure of spiritual profit. strip the glamour

of sheer scholarship from his interest in chinese philosophy, and what

remain? scarcely anything that the heir of western thought have not

pick up in his child’s copybook. and whilst he be waste his brain

and his moral energy and his physical strength in pursuit of the

shadow, the son of his loin, a human thing for whose moulding and

development he be, by the law of nature and civilization, responsible,

have grow up, haphazard, fatherless, motherless, under alien guidance.

he throw his memory back to his wife’s family, the Woodcotts,

narrow-minded, bigote, vulgar—Lord! how he have detest they. have he

abandon his son to their untender mercy? no matter who have train

the boy, he himself have fail in the most elementary duty of mankind.



suddenly he raise both clench fist and cry aloud:



“by God! I swear——”



then suddenly he see the ironical face of the village doctor of

Water-end and hear his sarcastic word: “a bad habit. I should give it

up”—and his arm drop helpless by his side. no. what be this oath

but one more irretrievable plunge into the morass in which he

flounder?



he begin again to wonder concern this newly discover son, strove to

visualize he. a broad, upstande fellow, like himself. Fairer—he get

that from his mother. a fine, soldierly figure in khaki. but only a

boy—just twenty. and he have throw everything to the wind on the

outbreak of war and have be fight in France—that child—for two

year. he draw a sharp breath, as a sudden thought smote he. the boy

might have be kill. apparently he be still alive. otherwise

sheepshank would surely have hear. but suppose—supposing. . . . he

shiver at the thought of it.



half an hour, an hour—he be unconscious of time—pass. then the door

open and Sheepshanks appear, follow by a short-bearded man in

clerical tweed.



“a bit of luck. I find Crosby in. I’ve tell he everything, and he have

be kind enough to come along.”



say Dr. Crosby a while later: “I have bring with I the boy’s last

letter—only a week old. perhaps you would like to see it.”



Baltazar stretch out an impatient hand. this thing so essentially

personal, the first objective token of his son’s existence, affect he

deeply. the word swam before his eye. he turn to the end to see the

signature. his thumb against it, he hold out the paper to sheepshank,

and say in a shake voice:



“that’s my handwriting. he have the same trick of the ‘b’ and the ‘z.’”



the letter inform the master that he be still at Churton Towers, near

Godalming; that the stump obstinately refuse to heal completely, owe

perhaps to the original gangrene; that he hope they would not chuck he

out of the Army, because, with a brand new foot, he could be useful in

hundred of way; but that, if they do, he would come up and continue

to read for his degree.



“may I keep this, Crosby?” ask Baltazar; and, permission give, he

fold it up and put it in his pocket. then he turn to sheepshank.

“why don’t you tell I at first what have happen?”



“my dear fellow,” say sheepshank, “I only hear he have be wound. I

be unaware of detail. that’s why I go at once to Crosby. in these

day one must be discreet.”



“yes, no doubt,” say Baltazar, absently. he pace the room for a few

moment. then halt: “I must see this son of mine. but I must see he

in my own way. will you do I a favour not to let he know of my

reappearance until I send you word?”



“certainly,” say Dr. Crosby.



“thank,” say he.



he walk to and fro, his head full of the tragedy of this maim young

life. he look from one unemotional face to the other. their attitude

be incomprehensible. Crosby, before show he the letter, have speak

of wound and amputation in the most matter-of-fact, unfeele way.

suddenly he burst out indignantly:



“I wonder if you two people have any idea of what I’m feel. to-day I

learn the wonderful news that I’ve get a son—a splendid fellow, a man

and a scholar. an hour afterwards you tell I that he’s a one-legged

cripple. neither of you seem to care a hang. I haven’t hear a word of

sympathy, of pity——”



the white-head, gold-spectacle senior tutor rush towards he, in

some agitation, with outspread hand.



“my dear J. B., we must observe a sense of proportion. you really ought

to go on your knee and thank God that your son be preserve to you.

he’s out of that hell for ever.”



“my boy—my only son—be kill last December,” say Dr. Crosby.



Baltazar stare for a moment at the short, bearded man and seek for

word, even the most conventional word; but they would not come. then,

memory flash on he, he stretch out his open hand about three foot

from the ground, and say, in a voice which sound queer in his own

ear:



“that little chap?”



“yes. that little chap,” say Dr. Crosby.









                              CHAPTER XII





A day or two afterwards Godfrey Baltazar, still tie by his maimed leg

to Churton Towers, receive a letter which cause he to frown and rub

his head. it be type-write save for the signature, and be address,

care of a firm of solicitor in Bedford row. as soon as Marcelle come to

do his morning dress he hand it to she.



“what do you make of this?”



before reply, she read it through without remark. it run:



      Dear Sir,



    _I have just be visit Cambridge after many year’ absence

    abroad, and have learn that the son of my old college friend,

    John Baltazar, be lie wound at Churton Towers Convalescent

    Home. I be write to you, therefore, to enquire whether one who

    be very intimately connect with your father in the old day

    might venture to run down to Godalming and see you, with the

    double purpose of make the acquaintance of John Baltazar’s

    son, of whose brilliant academic beginning the University

    authority have inform I, and of pay a strange

    Englishman’s tribute to a gallant fellow who have shed his blood

    for his country. my time be, at your disposal, I shall be

    happy to keep any appointment you may care to make._



                                      _your very faithfully_,

                                                       James Burden



“seem rather nice of he,” say Marcelle.



“I suppose it be. but who be the old fossil?”



Marcelle smile. “probably what he claim to be. an old college friend

of your father.”



“he must have be a don of sort. not merely an undergraduate friend.

otherwise how could he have get straight to the people who know all

about I? you ever hear of James Burden?”



“no,” reply Marcelle, shake her head. “how could I know all the

fellow of your father’s college? Newnham student in my day be keep

far from the mad crowd of don.”



“well, what about see the sentimental blighter? oh, of course he’s

sentimental. his ‘double purpose’ reek of it. rather what before the

war we use to call ‘colonial.’ what shall I do? shall I tell he to

come along?”



“why not? it can do no harm.”



Godfrey reflect for a few moment. then he say:



“you see, before I meet you I would have jump at the idea of see an

old friend of my father. but you know more of he than the whole lot of

the other put together. I’ve get my intimate picture of he through

you. I’m not so keen to get sidelight, possibly distort light, from

anybody else. you see what I mean, don’t you?”



“I see,” say Marcelle. “let we have a look at the foot.”



she ply her nurse’s craft; set he up for the day’s mild activity.

when he hobble an hour later into the hall to attend to his

correspondence and resume his study of the late Dr. Routh’s _treatise on

Rigid Dynamics_, he write a polite note to Mr. Burden suggest an

appointment. after all, even in such luxurious quarter as Churton

Towers, life be a bit monotonous, and straggler from the outer world

not unwelcome. it be all very well for most of his comrade, who have

mother, father, sister, cousin, girl friend attach and unattached

to visit they; but he, Godfrey, have find himself singularly alone. here

and there a representative of the Woodcott crowd have pay he a

perfunctory visit. he profess courteous appreciation. but they be

not his people. memory of his pariah boyhood discount their gush

over the one-footed hero with the Military Cross. he be cynical enough

to recognize that they take a vast lot of the credit to themselves, to

the Family. they go away puff with pride and promise. he say to

Marcelle:



“I’m not take any.”



a few man friend, chiefly man on leave, wander down from time to

time. but they have the same old tale to tell; of condition in the

sector, of change in the battalion, of such and such a scrap, of

promotion and death, a depressing devil of a lot of death; the

battalion ben’t what it be when Godfrey leave it; he could not imagine

the weird creature in Sam Browne belt that blow in from nowhere, to

take command of platoon, thing with their mother’s milk wet on their

lip, and garter from the Burlington Arcade, their idea of devilry, in

their pocket. and the N.C.O.s! my God! oh, for the good old day

of—six month ago!



Godfrey, wise in his generation, laugh at the jeremiad of these

callow _laudatore temporis acti_, and on probe far, satisfy

himself that everything be still for the good in the good of all

possible army. he also find that ginger be still hot in the mouth

of these friend of his, and that he have not live until he have see

Betty or Kitty or Elsie so-and-so, or such and such a Revue.



frankly and boyishly, his appreciate his friend’ entertain chatter.

but they come and go, with the superficial _bonhomie_ of the modern

soldier. they touch no depth. if he have die of his gangrened foot,

they would have say “poor old chap!” and think no more about he. he

do not condemn they, for he himself have say and think the same of

many a comrade who have go West. it be part of the game which he

play as scrupulously and as callously as the other. he crave,

however, solicitude deeply and more permanent.



of course there be Dorothy Mackworth. she do not come to Churton

Towers; but she have dutifully attend the Carlton when he have summon

her thither to meet Sister Baring, and put on for his benefit her most

adorable clothing and behaviour. the lunch have be a meal of delight.

the young man glow over his guest—the two prettiest woman, so he

declare, in the room. Marcelle in the much-admire hat, her cheek

slightly flushed and her eye bright, look absurdly young. the girl,

conscious of angelic dealing, carry off her own absurd youth with a

conquering air that bewitch he more than ever. she drop golden

word:



“oh, let we cut out Leopold! I’ve no use for he.”



she have no use for Leopold Doon, his half-brother and rival. he be to

be cut out of their happy thought. also:



“I’m not go to have you creep back into civil life and bury yourself

at Cambridge. you’d get a hump there you’d never recover from. there’s

lot of job on the staff for a brainy fellow like he, ben’t there,

Miss Baring? I’ll press father’s button and he’ll do the rest.”



now Dorothy’s father be a Major-General do thing at Whitehall,

whose nature be indicate by mystic capital letter after his name.



“you’ll look splendid in red tab,” she add.



this profession of interest and this air of proprietorship enrapture

he. under the ban of her displeasure Cambridge fade into a dreary,

tumbledown desolation. she have but to touch he with her fairy wand and

he would break out all over in red tab. she speak with assurance in the

future tense.



and again, in a low voice, on their wind way out through the table

of the restaurant, Marcelle precede they by a yard or two:



“Miss Baring’s a real dear. but don’t fall in love with she, for I swear

I’m not go to play gooseberry.”



he have protest in a whisper: “fall in love with anyone but you?”



and she have reply: “I think I’m nice enough,” and have laugh at he

over her shoulder and look exceedingly desirable.



he have never dare till that inspire moment speak to she of love in

plain, bald term; now he have do it and not only remain unfrozen,

but bask in the warmth of her approval.



“I think that’s the most beautiful beano I’ve ever have,” he say to

Marcelle, on their journey back to Godalming.



yes. there be Dorothy. she have promise to participate in a similar

beano any time he like. but such bright occurrence must be rare. he

long to plunge into fervid correspondence. caution restrain he.

elusive and perplexing, Heaven know what she might say to a violent

declaration of passion. it might ruin a state of thing both delicate

and delicious. far well carry on his wooing by word of mouth.



in the meanwhile, the day at Churton Towers be long and life lack

variety. so he look forward to the visit of Mr. James Burden, compound

of fossil and sentimental blighter though he might be.



                 *        *        *        *        *



Punctually at three o’clock, the appoint hour, one afternoon, the maid

who attend the door come up to Godfrey Baltazar wait lonely in the

great hall, and announce the visitor. with the aid of the now familiar

crutch he rise nimbly. he see advance towards he in a brisk, brusque

way, a still young-look man in grey tweed, rather above medium

height, thickset, give an immediate impression of physical strength.



“be you Mr. Godfrey Baltazar?”



“yes, sir,” say the boy courteously.



“my name be Burden. it’s good of you to let I come to see you.”



he grasp Godfrey’s hand in a close grip and look at he keenly out

of bright grey eye. not much fossil there, think the young man. on

the contrary, a singularly live personality. there be strength in the

heavy though clean-cut face, mark by the deep vertical furrow between

the brow; strength in the coarse, though well-trim, thatch of brown

hair unstreaked by grey; strength in his voice.



“do sit down,” say Godfrey.



Baltazar sit down and, look at his son, clutch the arm of his

chair. Crosby and Sheepshanks be right. a splendid fellow, the ideal

of a soldier, clean run, clear eye; a touch of distinction and breed

about he, manifestation of the indomitable old Huguenot strain. by God!

a boy to be proud of; and he see bit of himself in the boy’s feature,

expression and gesture. a thrill run through he as he drink in the new

joy of parenthood. yet through the joy pain stab he—fierce

resentment against Fate, which have cheat he of the wonderful year of

the boy’s growth and development. for the first time in his decisive

life he feel tongue-tie and embarrassed. he curse the craftiness that

bring he hither under an assumed name. yet, have he write as John

Baltazar, he would have risk a rebuff. what sentimental regard or

respect could this young man have for his unknown and unnatural father?

at any rate his primary object have be attain. here he be in his

son’s presence, a courteously welcome guest. he look at he with

yearn eye; Godfrey meet his gaze with cool politeness. Baltazar wipe

a perspiring brow. after a few moment Godfrey break an awkward

situation by offer his cigarette case. the cigarette light, Baltazar

say suddenly:



“it’s an infernal shame!”



“what?” ask Godfrey, startle.



Baltazar point downwards. “that,” say he.



“oh!” Godfrey laugh. “I’m one of the lucky one. far well to have

stop it with my foot than my head.”



“but to limp about on crutch all your life—a fellow like you in the

pride of youth and strength. it make one angry.”



“that’s kind of you, sir,” say Godfrey. “but it don’t worry I much.

they’re wangle a new foot for I, and as soon as I can stick it on,

I’ll throw away my crutch, and no one but myself will be a bit the

wiser.”



“you take it bravely,” say Baltazar.



“it’s all in the day’s work. what’s the good of grousing? what’s the

point of a real foot, anyway, when a fake one will do as well?”



but though Baltazar admire the young fellow’s careless courage, he

still glower at the maimed leg. he resent fiercely the lost foot. he

have be rob of a bit of this wonderful son.



“how do you come to get hit?” he ask abruptly.



there be many way of ask a wound man such a question. many he

loathe. hence the savagely facetious answer that have be put on

record. but there be way that compel reply. Baltazar’s be one.

Godfrey felt strangely affect by the eld man’s earnestness; yet his

instinct forbid he to yield at once.



“getting hit’s as simple as be bowl out at cricket. a jolly sight

simple. like go out in the rain and get wet. you just go out

without an umbrella and something hit you, and that’s the end of it.”



“but when be it? how be it?” ask Baltazar.



Godfrey, after the way of british subaltern, give a bald account of his

personal adventure in his last fight near Ypres. it might have be a

description of a football match. Baltazar wonder. for all his

wandering and experience of life, he have never hear a first-hand

account of modern warfare. the psychology of it perplex and fascinate

he. he ply the young man with question; shrewd, direct question

pierce to the heart of thing; and gradually Godfrey’s English reserve

melt, and he lay aside his defensive armour and tell his intent

visitor what he want to know. and Baltazar’s swift brain seize the

vivid picture and co-ordinate they until he grow aware of the hell

through which this young and debonair gentleman have pass.



“and what do you get that for?”



he point to the ribbon of the Military Cross.



“I manage to get away with some machine gun out of a tight corner. it

be only when we be scoot back that I discover we have be leave

in the air. I think the battalion be quite up close. if I haven’t, I

should probably have bolt. these thing be all fluke.”



“what a proud man your father would have be,” say Baltazar.



“by the way, yes,” say Godfrey. “I be forget. you be a friend of

my father’s.”



“it’s a great misfortune that he never meet you,” say Baltazar.



“he disappear before I be bear,” Godfrey remark drily.



“I know. that’s why I write to you in some diffidence. I have no idea how

you regard your father’s memory. I hope you appreciate my feeling that

I might be treading on delicate ground.”



Godfrey wave an indulgent hand. “oh, that’s all right, sir. my father

be a distinguished and romantic person, and I’m rather interested in

he than otherwise.”



Baltazar draw a great breath of relief. at any rate he be not execrate

by the paragon of son. “I see,” say he, his feature relax, for the

first time, into a smile. “like any other ancestor, he’s part of your

family history.”



“something of the sort. only perhaps a bit near.”



“how nearer?”



“People live who know he in the flesh. you, for instance.”



“yes,” say Baltazar. “I know he intimately. we be undergraduate and

don together. I leave Cambridge about the same time as he do—when my

fellowship lapse. I go away to the Far East, where I’ve spend my

life. I’m just back, you know. Instinct take I to Cambridge, a sort of

Rip van Winkle, to see if there be any remain of old friend—and my

visit to you be the result of my enquiry.”



“when you write to I, I wonder whether you could tell I if my father

be alive or dead.”



Baltazar make a little gesture.



“_Quien sabe?_ from what I remember of John Baltazar he be not a man to

let himself die easily. he be the most obstinate mule I ever come

across. death would have have a try time with he. besides, he be as

tough as a rhinoceros.”



“so he still may be in the land of the living?”



“as far as I know.” Baltazar lean forward on his chair. “you have no

feeling of resentment against he?”



“one cann’t feel resentment against a shadow,” reply Godfrey.



“suppose he reappear, what would be your attitude towards he?”



Godfrey frown at the touch of impertinence in the question which

probe too deeply. he glance distrustfully at his visitor.



“I’m afraid I’ve never consider the point,” he reply frostily. “have

you any special reason for put it to I?”



Baltazar wince. “only as a student of psychology. but I see you would

rather continue to regard he as a legendary character?”



“quite,” say Godfrey.



“you must forgive I, Mr. Baltazar,” say the father, with a smile. “I’m

half orientalize and only begin to attune myself to western habit

of thought. I live for so many year in the interior of China that I

almost lose the western point of view. well, there the basis of all

religious and philosophic system be filial piety. the whole moral and

political system of the Empire have be rear on it for thousand of

year. if you be a Chinaman, you would venerate your father, no matter

what grievance you might have against he or how shadowy and legendary

he might be.”



“but I’m not a Chinaman,” say Godfrey.



“precisely. that’s where your typically western point of view be of

great interest to I. I hope, therefore, you see that the question I put

to you, although it may be one of curiosity, be of philosophical and not

idle curiosity.”



“I see,” reply Godfrey, smile and mollify. “may I ask you which of

the two attitude you consider the most workable in practical life?”



“I tell you just now,” say Baltazar, “that my mind be in process of

adjustment.”



there come a slight pause. Godfrey break it by suggest politely that

Mr. Burden must have find Cambridge greatly change. Baltazar launch

into vivid description of the toga give way to arm. eventually come

to personality. the death of Dr. Crosby’s only son.



“yes. I hear,” say Godfrey. “fine soldier. do in by high explosive

shell. not a trace of he or six other leave. not even the heel of a

boot.”



“how lightly you all take death nowadays,” Baltazar remark

wonderingly.



“that oughtn’t to surprise you,” say Godfrey. “I’ve be lead to believe

they don’t worry their head much about it in China.”



“I think it one of the point at which East and West could never

touch.” he laugh. “more readjustment, you see.”



“in the Army we’ve get either to be fatalist or lunatic. if your

number’s up it’s up, and that’s all there be to it. _you_ cann’t do

anything. you cann’t even run away.”



“but surely you cling to life—young man like you—with all sort of

golden promise in front of you?”



“we don’t do silly ass thing,” say Godfrey. “we don’t stand about like

Ajaxes defy the lightning. when shell come we scurry like rabbit

into the near funk-hole. we’re not a bit brave unless there’s no help

for it. but when you see so many people kill around you, you say ‘my

turn next,’ and it don’t seem to matter. you think ‘who the blaze be

you that you should be so precious?’ . . . no. go out all in the

fraction of a second like Crosby don’t matter. why should it? what

do give you a horrible feeling in the pit of your stomach be the fear

lest you may be utterly mess up and go on living. but death itself be

too damned ordinary. at any rate, that’s the way I size it up. of course

it’s pretty cheap and easy for a lucky beggar like I, who’s out of it

for ever, to talk hot philosophic air—but all the same, look back, I

think I’ve tell you in a vague sort of way what I feel when I be out in

France. sometimes the whole thing seem a nightmare. at other, I want

to kick myself for sit here in luxury when there’s so much to be

do out there. I have get my platoon—I be act first

lieutenant—like a high-class orchestra—just the last two month, you

know. it be the weird feeling. I just have to wave my baton and they

do everything I want. once or twice I nearly cry with sheer

amazement. and then just when the band be play its damnd, I get

knock out and faint like a silly fool, and wake up mile away. when

one have sweat one’s gut out over a thing, it’s annoying not to reap

the fruit of it. it’s rough luck. It’s—well——”



suddenly self-consciousness return. he flush deeply.



“I’m awfully sorry, sir. I never mean to bore you like this about

myself.”



“bore I!” cry Baltazar. “my dear fellow, you could go on like this

for ever and command my most amazed interest. do go on.”



“it’s very kind of you,” stammer the young man, “but—really——”



he stop, confused, embarrassed, ashamed of his boasting. never have he

speak like that to human being of his incomparable platoon. never have

he unveil to profane eye his soldier’s Holy of Holies. certainly not

to his comrade. not to Dorothy. not even to Marcelle. what on earth

must this stranger, whom he don’t know from Adam, be think of he?

he light a cigarette, before, remember manner, he offer his case to

his visitor. the sense of sentimental braggadocio overwhelm he,

burn he red-hot. he long with sudden fury to get rid of this

uncanny guest with his clear, compelling eye, which even now steadily

regard he with an inscrutable smile and continue the impossible

invitation: “do go on.” he could no more go on than smite he over the

head with his crutch (which he be far more inclined to do) for pluck

out the heart of his mystery. if only the man would go! but he sit

there, strong, urbane, maddeningly kind. he hate he. yet he feel

himself under his influence. from the man seem to emanate a suggestion

of friendship, interest, control, which his sensitive English spirit

vehemently repudiate. he hear he say:



“the old french blood in your vein have suddenly come up against the

English.”



he start. “what do you know about my french ancestry?”



“your father be very proud of his Huguenot descent.”



“my father!” cry Godfrey, his nerve on edge. “I’m rather feed up with

my father. I wish he have never be bear.”



Baltazar rise. “I’m sorry,” say he courteously, “to have distress

you. believe I, it be far from my intention.”



Godfrey stare at he for a second, and pass his hand across his eye.



“it’s for I to apologize. I’m afraid I’ve be rude. please don’t go.”



but Baltazar stand smile, hold out his hand. now that the man be

go Godfrey realize the enormity of his own discourtesy. he look

around as if seek some outlet for the situation. and then, as if in

answer to a prayer, at the end of the hall appear the passing,

grey-clothe figure of a guardian angel.



“Sister!” he cry.



Marcelle halt, smile, and advance towards he.



“Sister,” say he, “this be Mr. James Burden. you ought to know each

other. you both know my father.”



Baltazar turn. and for a few speechless second he and Marcelle stare

into each other’s eye.









                              CHAPTER XIII





godfrey half rise from his chair, more than puzzle by the mutual

recognition.



“you say you don’t know Mr. Burden,” he cry.



but neither heed he. Baltazar make a stride forward and with one hand

grip Marcelle by the arm and with the other motioned in his imperious

way to the open door. still look at he in wonderment, she allow

he to lead she quickly to the terrace at the head of the step.

Godfrey’s astonish gaze follow they till they disappear. outside,

Baltazar release she.



“Marcelle! what in thunder be you do here?”



she be too greatly overwhelmed to reply. she could only gasp a few

broken and foolish word.



“you? John Baltazar? alive?”



“never be less dead. but you! you of all people. my God! although I

lose you, I could never lose your face. it have be with I all the

time. and there it be, the same as ever. but what be you do here?”



she make a vague gesture over her costume.



“I’m a professional nurse. sister-in-charge. I’ve be nurse all my

life.”



“not when I know you,” say Baltazar.



“my life begin after that.”



“marry?”



the colour come back into her white cheek. “no,” she say.



“neither be I.”



he put both hand on her shrink shoulder and bent on her eye which

she could not meet.



“you at last, after all these year! just the same. just as beautiful.

much more.”



“this be rather public,” she manage to say, release herself. “there

be lot of patient——”



he laugh and, indicate the parapet, invite she to sit.



“you must forgive I,” he say, seat himself by her side. “the sight

of you blot out the world. don’t be frighten. I’m quite tame now.

look at I.”



she obey he as she have do in her early girlhood, dominate for the

moment by his tone.



“how do you think I’m look? batter by time? a crock to be wrap

up in flannel and set in the chimney-corner to wheeze the rest of his

life away?”



“you look very little old,” she say with a wan smile. “and you

haven’t a grey hair in your head.”



“that’s good. I’m as young as ever I be. I can sweep away twenty year

and begin where I leave off.”



“you’re more fortunate than I be,” say Marcelle.



“Rubbish!” say Baltazar.



she glance at he wistfully and then out over the tree.



“nursing ben’t the road to perpetual youth,” she say. then lest he

should catch up her word, she continue swiftly: “but you must tell I

where you have be, how you’ve come back to life. you disappear

utterly. you never write. if we all think you dead, be it our fault?

when Godfrey show I your letter, I never dream who James Burden

might be.”



“Godfrey?” Baltazar pounce on the name. “do you call he Godfrey? then

you must be old friend. hence the miracle of find you together. have

you be mother he all his life?”



she shake her head. “how you jump at conclusion! no. I meet he for the

first time when I come here—a month ago.”



“so it’s just Chance, Fate, Destiny, the three of we meeting like this?

the hand of God? . . . wait, though. I cann’t see quite clearly. you

learn he be my son?”



she smile again:



“do you think we call all young officer here by their christian name?”



“do he know that you know I?”



“if he don’t,” she reply, “he wouldn’t have consult I about Mr.

Burden’s letter. I wish I have be mother he all his life,” she

add after a pause; “but I’ve be do my good for the last month. I

cann’t help love he.”



“what do he know about you and I?”



“I’ve tell he everything,” say Marcelle.



Baltazar start to his foot.



“then when he see we gape at each other just now, he must have

guess, or he cann’t have any Baltazar brain in his head.” he move

away a pace; then turn on she. “you give I a good character?”



her head be bow. she do not see the rare laughter in his eye, but

take his question seriously.



“can you doubt it?” she beckon he nearer, and say in a low voice: “I

may have be wrong, but I have give he to understand that it be

entirely on my account—you know what I mean——”



“what other reason, in the name of God could I have have?” he exclaim

with a large gesture.



if there have linger a doubt in her mind, the note of sincerity in the

man’s cry would have drive it away for ever. it awake a harmonic chord

of gladness in her heart and her whole be vibrate. although John

Baltazar’s subsequent career be as yet dark and mysterious, her faith,

at least, be justify. she say without look at he:



“you’ll find that I’ve be loyal.”



he stride towards she and, disregard the peril of publicity, again

take she by the shoulder.



“what kind of a cynical beast do you think I’ve turn into?”



he sweep away, leave she physically conscious of the impress of his

finger in her flesh and her brain reeling.



                 *        *        *        *        *



Baltazar march into the great hall to Godfrey, still sit in his

“good-bye.”

“he’s quite right. I need a little time to get use to it.”

the beech foliage be just begin to turn faint golden. here and

“to be interested in a legendary sort of father be one thing. there’s

“a queer devil!” say Godfrey. “do you know what he suggest to I? a

he’d buck it up.”









                              CHAPTER XIV





CAMBRIDGE put Baltazar on the track of old acquaintance, so that on his

return to London he find himself in contact with people of his own

standing who could explain to he the contemporary attitude of mind.

there be Burtingshaw, K.C., for instance, a member of the Inventions

well.”

Comfortable Mrs. Jackman smilingly agree. without doubt that be the

“not since we’ve be in uniform.”



“by Jove, that’s true!” he point to the M.C. ribbon. “splendid, old

chap, glorious!”



“glory all right,” laugh Godfrey, “but,” point downward, “_sic

transit_——”



“oh, hell!” say the other.



“Kinnaird,” say Godfrey, “let I introduce you to my father.”



Baltazar beam. his quick eye gather curious glance from the

luncheon party. it be a proud moment, inaugurate a definite parental

position. he wring the young man’s hand cordially. Godfrey explain:

“Kinnaird and I be at Winchester and Cambridge together. he’s a

classical swell. when the war come it swallow we up with different

mouth.” he turn to his friend. “where have you be all the time?”



“Gallipoli. then a soft turn in Egypt. and you?”



“Flanders and France.”



“I’m off to France next week.”



“let we meet before you go. where be you to be find?”



they exchange address. on leave-taking:



“I’m proud to have meet you, sir,” say Kinnaird. he turn and sit down

at his table. Father and son continue their way to the lounge.



“be that last remark of your friend,” ask Baltazar, “unusual

politeness, or do it mean anything?”



“Most of my University friend, sir,” reply Godfrey, “know who my

father be.”



“oh!” say Baltazar, with knit brow. “oh, indeed! anyhow it be very

polite. look here, my boy,” he go on, as they halt by a seclude and

invite little table, “I’ve be strike lately by an outward and

visible sign of what seem to I to be an inward, invisible grace. when

I be your age, having leave school and master behind I, I would have

see anybody damn first before I call they ‘sir’—except royalty, of

course. now I come back into the world as an elderly codger, and both of

you young chap ‘sir’ I punctiliously.”



“I suppose the Army be teach we manner,” say Godfrey.



“then the war be of some good, after all,” comment Baltazar. “and this

reversion to an ancient code provide you with a mode of address which

save you, my young friend, from considerable embarrassment.”



Godfrey, quick and sensitive, glance for an instant at the firm lip

draw down in a humorous smile and at the kindly indulgence in the keen

eye, and then break into a laugh.



“let we be grateful, sir, to the _Chinoiserie_ of the eighteenth

century.”



Baltazar fold his arm and contemplate his son admiringly.



“do you know, I couldn’t have get out of it like that if I have think

for a thousand year. let we sit down.” and when they have settle

themselves by the wall on the fringe of the crowded lounge, he go on:

“you young man be not the least problem which a Cyrano drop from the

peaceful moon like myself have to solve.”



“I’m afraid we don’t quite know what we’re play at ourselves,” say

Godfrey.



again Baltazar feel pleased with the boy’s reply. an understanding

fellow; one who could get to the thought behind a few word.



“I wish to God I have know you all your life,” say he.



at the appeal to sentiment, Godfrey shy like a horse.



“it wouldn’t have affect what the war have make of I. I should have

join up just the same, and, just the same, I should have have a hell of

a time in a perpetual blue funk which I have to hide, and should have

come out minus a foot; and just the same too I should have wonder how

on earth I’m go to stick the University—if I do go back—with its

childish little rule and restriction—to say nothing of its limited

outlook.”



“two or three year ago,” say Baltazar, follow his son’s lead, “if I

hear a fellow of twenty talk about the limited outlook of the

University of Cambridge, I should have say that his proper sphere be

the deep inferno of insufferable young prig provide by another

ancient seat of learn situate also on the bank of a river. as your

tutor, I should have have even nasty and more sarcastic thing than

that to say to you. but now, in this new and incomprehensible world, I’m

perfectly ready to agree with you. what be there of the conduct or

meaning of life that our dear old pragmatical drake of a Crosby and his

train of duck can teach man like your friend Kinnaird and yourself?

it’s like a bunch of hare sit down before an old tortoise and be

teach how to run. ben’t that the way of it?”



“I suppose it be,” reply Godfrey, laugh. “I don’t want to crab man

like the master. nothing can take away their scholarship, which, after

all, be vital to human progress—and, of course, as far as that go,

I’m perfectly willing to sit at their foot—but—well—I know you see

what I mean, sir. it’s very jolly of you, as one of the eld crowd, and

very unusual, to be so sympathetic.”



“I’ll go far than that,” say Baltazar. “as one of the eld crowd,

I should like to have the benefit of your concentrated experience of

modern life, and that be why I propose to tell you my story of Spendale

Farm, Quong Ho, and the Zeppelin. it’s my Ancient Mariner’s tale, and

you cannot choose but hear. but for the Lord’s sake tell what you can

remember of it to Sister Baring, for I’m sick to death of it.”



                 *        *        *        *        *



it be nearly five o’clock when he have finish. find Godfrey a

sensitive listener, he have expound with many picturesque and intimate

detail the story which he have roughly tell so often. the reason for his

sudden self-condemnation to exile he have gloss over, as he have do

when first he have account for himself to sheepshank. oddly enough, no

one, not even this son of his, with the quick insight force to maturity

by the hot-house of war, boggle at the reason. all accept his

maniacal proceeding as in keep with the impulsive eccentricity of his

career. besides, the mere fact of a man be able so to eliminate from

his surrounding every whisper of the outside world as to live in

England and remain in absolute ignorance of the war for a couple of

year, stagger credulity and eclipse minor consideration.



“well,” say Baltazar, with a big gesture of both arm, “that’s how it

be. to sum up. eighteen year’ blank ignorance of, and indifference to,

european history—political, social, moral, artistic, scientific. a

week’s dismay and disgust. two year’ seclusion devote to the

consolidation of my life’s work. the whole thing wipe out in a night.

awakening to find the world have be at war for two year. myself adrift

in a sort of typhoon, with not a human straw to cling to but my adopt

son, this extraordinary mathematical genius of a Quong Ho. I fly to

Cambridge to try to get some sort of sane attachment to life. I discover

your existence. no soon do I meet you than I’m throw against the very

woman for whose sake, as a young man, I chuck the whole of my career.

and here be I, as strong as a horse. feel that”—he tender his arm and

brace his muscle, and Godfrey grip it proclaim, with wonder, that

it be like an iron bar—“and with a first-class working brain, and the

country be cry out both for brain and muscle, and I’ll go mad if I

don’t give the country my good. but at the same time, I’m just a

month-old child. I’m daze by everything. and I’ve get you and Marcelle

and Quong Ho to look after. you’re all inextricably weave into the

tapestry of my life. Mathematics and chinese scholarship can go to the

devil. only the four of you matter——”



“Four?” Godfrey query.



“yes. four. you, Marcelle, Quong Ho, and England.”



“that’s a tall order, sir,” smile Godfrey. “but as for I, I’m all

right. I can fend for myself. you can cut I out.”



Baltazar bring down his hand with a great thump on the little table.



“I’m damn if I do!” and to the waiter who run up in some alarm: “yes,

tea. China tea. gallon of it.”









                               CHAPTER XV





BALTAZAR have ask his friend Burtingshaw, K.C., to suggest some sphere

in which his gift might be usefully employ by the nation.

Burtingshaw, an unimaginative fellow, a professional exploiter of

formula, bid he become a special constable and join the National

Volunteers. the man all agog to save his country, scoff at the advice.

if there be march to be do and blow to be strike, he have far

well enlist. just like a Chancery lawyer to try to damp enthusiasm. he

decide to bide his time, to adopt the unusual course of look before

he leap. to judge by what he could gather from the press and from

conversation, it have be the cry fault of the Government from the

beginning of the war to use razor to cut butter and wooden blade to

perform delicate operation. there must be wait in the vast war

machine one particular lever which he of all man be qualified to pull.

to find it would take time. but what be it? Godfrey’s suggestion run

from vague to gloomy. possibly he could find a billet in one of the new

ministry spring up like mushroom every day, or he might de

Y.M.C.A. work, or drive a motor ambulance in France. all of which be as

satisfactory to the perfervid patriot as the idea of join the Special

Constabulary or the National Volunteer Force. he rebel at

half-measure.



meanwhile, his own house have first to be set in order. he begin

operation by remove his worldly good (easily contain in one

suit-case and a large brown-paper package) to a comfortable hotel at

Godalming, so as to be near Godfrey and Marcelle. the quiet, too, of a

private sitting-room in a country inn conduce to the prosecution of

certain study which Professor Weatherley, admirable guide in the

world-welter, have recommend. he take up his quarter the most

contented and sanguine of man. he have receive a letter from Quong Ho,

in faultless, ciceronian English, convey the news that he be well

forward on the road to complete recovery, and in a few day would be in

a fit condition to pursue whatever course of action his most venerate

master might choose to prescribe. when he have dispose the book and

pamphlet, content of the brown-paper package, about his room, he sit

down and write to Quong Ho. a room in the Godalming hotel be at Quong

Ho’s disposal as soon as he be fit to travel. it would be an admirable

opportunity for he to meet Godfrey. they be to be brother, mutually

helpful: Godfrey, a past-master in the science of modern life but a

neophyte in mathematic, see that he be struggle with such

childish puzzle as the element of Rigid Dynamics; Quong Ho, on the

other hand, a neophyte in the science of modern life, but a past-master

in elementary mathematic. it be important, he write, that Quong Ho’s

appearance should, as far as possible, be thoroughly european and his

dress impeccable.



“Good Lord!” he cry aloud, throw down his pen. “I clean forgot. the

poor beggar haven’t a rag to his back!”



he draft a telegram to the tailor firm in the cathedral city,

instruct they to supply Mr. Ho with essential raiment, and then,

continue his epistle to his pupil, give he safe counsel and his

blessing, and enclose a cheque to meet necessary expense.



after which he lunch in the coffee-room with the appetite of the

healthy man, lounge for a while with a pipe on the tranquil pavement

outside the inn, and then go upstairs again, throw himself contentedly

into an arm-chair with a german war publication lend he by Weatherley,

and wait for Marcelle.



                 *        *        *        *        *



it be her afternoon of freedom. she have look forward to the interview

with mingled longing and apprehension. he have be the only man in her

life, and it be all such a long time ago. the jealous grip of her

nurse’s work have fasten upon neck and shoulder, and bent the

concentration of she be within a succession of little horizon. man

she have meet and know intimately, man in thousand; but they be all

suffer man, man whose sole appeal to her womanhood be their

helplessness, their dependence. if there cross her path a man with

strong protective arm and compelling eye, he be whisk away sound and

whole beyond her horizon’s misty rim. now and then, but rarely, in

haggard face shine eye of desire. her sex revolt until experience

teach she the nurse’s cynical indifference. of course there be the

romance of nursing. in her long career she have know of many; of many,

too, in which the resultant marriage have be all that be adumbrate by

the end of the fairy tale. but no ghost of such a romance have ever

come her way. and no romance have come her way in her restrict social

life. her holiday have be too rare and fleeting. here and there,

perhaps, a man have be attract by her good look and her

graciousness, but before these have have time to consolidate a first

effect, she be mile away, back again in uniform between the eternal

row of bed. she have work hard and seriously, the perfect nurse,

accept, without question, the hospital ward as the sphere ordain

for she by destiny. yet to soften the rigid life, she have foster in

her heart the memory of the brief and throb love of long ago.



during her drive from Churton Towers in the motor-cab, foolish

trepidation beset she. although her woman of the world’s sound sense

make mock of timidity, yet old-maidish instinct question the

propriety of her proceeding. she be go to meet her former lover in a

private room of an hotel. what about professional decorum? Matron, who

keep a hard and unsympathetic eye on flirtatious tendency in the

junior staff, would regard her visit, should she come to know of it, as

a horrifying escapade. she have see she as she run down the step,

hat, gloved, prink to her good, with a betraying flush (lobster

colour, she think) on her cheek; and be within earshot of the

Gorgon, she have throw the mere word “Godalming” at the chauffeur as she

enter the car. when she gather up courage to look at herself in the

strip of mirror that face she, her prejudiced eye see herself pale and

haggard, smite with line which she have not notice when she put on

her hat. and all the time she know that these feminine preoccupation

be but iridescence on the surface of deep, black water fill with

fear, and that she be let her mind play on they so as not to think

of the depth.



Baltazar be wait for she outside the hotel. thus one little fear be

send packing. as a nurse she would have go to Hell Gates to enquire

for a man. she have do it many a time in France. as Marcelle Baring she

be restrain by futile hesitancy. as Marcelle Baring, a woman with

her own life to lead, she be unfamiliar to herself. she have shrink from

enter the inn alone and ask for Mr. Baltazar. but there he be

there never have be a tryst hard or venturesome for she to keep, never

one on which he be not there before she, big, responsible, inspire

confidence. he be singularly unchanged.



obey a breezy wave of the hand, she sink into an arm-chair. he shut

the door and cross the room, his face light with happiness.



“for the first time in our life we’re together alone within four wall.

you and I. ben’t it strange? we have to talk. not only now, but often.

as often as we can. it would have be monstrous of I to expect you to

run up and down to London. besides, there would have be no privacy.

the lounge of the great hotel—I loathe they! a man and woman sit

whispering in a corner and at once surround themselves with an

atmosphere of intrigue. horrible! and I couldn’t come every day to

Churton tower—even ostensibly to see Godfrey. there would have be

the devil to pay. all sort of scandal. so I’ve make this my

headquarters, in order to be near you.”



the weather have turn raw and cold, and as she have drive in an open

car, clothe in light coat and skirt, with nothing to warm she but a fur

smile, and say it be very cosy. he search the room for a hassock,

and find one set it beneath her foot.



“we’ll have tea soon, which will make it cosier,” he say. he throw

himself into an arm-chair on the other side of the fire. “it’s like a

fairy-tale, ben’t it?”



she admit the strangeness of the circumstance in which they have meet,

and with instinct of self-defence begin to speak of Godfrey, of their

“cann’t you realize what you’ve be to I? ‘all a wonder and a wild

desire!’”

say to you. then we lose our head and break off a delightful

“how can we go back twenty year?”



“by wipe out two hundred and forty unimportant month from our

she glance up at he and shake her head. it be the grey and barren

necessary to recapture the grace of those brief and exquisite moment.

“it’s very easy to play with word and metaphor and analogy. you can

Baltazar put his hand in his pocket, laugh, turn away, and sit

“we seem to have get on to the basis of a nice and interminable

if I’m anything at all, I’m a man of illimitable patience.”



she laugh out loud. she could not help it. a typhoon proclaim its

Zephyrdom! and proclaim it not jestingly, but with the accent of

deeply rooted conviction.



“you? you patient? oh, my dear——”



“there,” he cry, jump up from his chair. “you have call I ‘my

dear’!”



quickly she retort: “I don’t. at least, I don’t mean to. you catch

I up in your patient way. I be go to call you my dear something—my

dear sir—my dear man——”



“my name happen to be John,” say Baltazar.



“‘my dear John’? no. I ben’t go to say that.”



“why?”



“it sound as if we have be marry for twenty year.”



with feminine instinct she have put her foot on his man’s vanity and have

use it, like a rock climber, as a projection to mount to safety. she

“I suppose you’re right,” say Baltazar. “it’s a damned name. it’s

whereat they both laugh, and the situation, as far as it affect she,

“Damn the Huns for rob I of my tea!” he cry, “besides damn

Marcelle flash a protest. “they haven’t. they’re incapable of it. I’ve

be in France, in the thick of it, close up to the Front—and I’ve see

thing. I know. they haven’t do one good thing.”



“they have,” say Baltazar. “they’ve bring you and I together.”



“oh!” say Marcelle rather foolishly. “I think you be refer to

he fasten on the word. “serious? do you suppose that your presence

here at this minute, with that little bite-into piece of buttered

she drop the bit of toast into her saucer and regard he with

“why spoil everything? we be begin to get along so nicely.”

in distress, she reply: “what you mustn’t say again. if you do, it’s

“oh, no, no!” her voice quiver and she sink back in her chair, with

she answer wearily: “I’ve tell you. the year that the locust hath

eat.”



“what locust?”



“ah!” she sigh.

shoulder.



“my dear,” say he tenderly, “forgive I. I ought to have think of it

else—since——? well, there haven’t. I’ve be far too busy.” and see

for the moment she wish there have be an intervene lover whose

memory she could use as a rampart, for again she feel defenceless. if

Laughter like quick sunshine light his face. “a thousand pardon,

tea, I mean—not be with you.”



she breathe again, rather wonder at the power of a light word. of

Hitherto she have regard man sick with maternal indulgence. be she to

hand she the covered china dish from the warm hob.



“not that unsacramental bit of bread,” he cry.



it be not do rudely or bearishly; it be do in the most charming

he have not change. it be she who have change. the fault lie in

make some sort of amend.



there remain but a quarter of an hour before Godfrey be due. she light

a cigarette from the match which Baltazar hold out.



“I wonder,” she say, with a little air of deliberation, “whether you

would let I say something—and remain quite quiet?”



he reply happily: “I swear I’ll sit in this chair until you give I

leave to get up. but why say it? you’ve never let I finish what I want

to tell you. it have to be tell now, or a month or six month or a year

long sleep to find myself in a world of marvel, in a new, throb
