once. I’ve be pursue shadow for half a century. I want to get into

the substance of life at last. a man cann’t do it by himself. he need a

woman, just as—to advance an abstract proposition—a woman need a man.

you’re the only woman in the world for I. together, you and I, we can

go forth strong into this wonderful conflict. you can help I, I can

help you. if you’re tired and want rest, by God, you shall have it. you

shalln’t do a hand’s turn. but a smile and a whisper from you will fill I

with strength for both of we. that’s the proposition.”



she look for a long time into the fire, her head aslant, her lip and

finger accompany her thought in nervous movement. presently she

say, in a low voice:



“a man like you would want the Sun, Moon and Stars.”



“and would see that he get they,” say Baltazar. “they’re there right

enough.”



she shake her head despairingly.

give—what ben’t in I to give. don’t you see it’s no good? the whole

thing be dead. I think it be alive, but it ben’t. it’s dead. I’m

dead. I suppose a nurse’s work eventually unsex a woman. that’s frank

“it’s a frank statement of a conclusion arrive at through fallacious

reasoning,” reply Baltazar.



she shiver. “these thing have nothing to do with reason. in all these

year haven’t you learn that?”



“no,” say he. “Schopenhauer and his lot be idiot. love be the

apotheosis of reason. my dear,” he add, rise, “this be profitless

through, my dear, from your lip to your heart. perhaps I’ve be rather

like a bull at a gate—the gate of heaven. I suppose I be build like

that. but if you’ll let we be friend, dear friend, I willn’t worry you

any more. I promise.”



she break down. tear come.



“I’m so sorry—so sorry. but you do understand, don’t you?”



“I don’t say I understand, my dear,” he reply very tenderly. “but I

accept the phenomenon.”



he turn and look out of the window at the quiet road. presently a

taxi-cab draw up outside.



“here’s Godfrey,” he say.



she rise. “I’ll go down and meet he. it’s no use his climb all these

difficult stair.”



“you’ll come again, willn’t you?” and see a flicker of hesitation pass

over her face, he add: “if only to let I show you Quong Ho.”



“yes, I’ll come again,” she reply, “if only to show you——”



“what?”



“that I’m sorry.”



she move quickly to the door, which he open, and he follow she

downstair. in the vestibule they meet Godfrey. gloom overspread the

young man’s candid face and dejection mark his behaviour, neither of

which could be account for by the fact of the Medical Board having

give he, as he announce, a further two month. baltazar’s proposal to

run over soon to Churton Towers for a talk, he welcome with polite lack

of enthusiasm. he take leave with the solemnity of a medical man

depart from a house with a corpse in it.



“it don’t seem to be one of the House of Baltazar’s lucky day,” say

Baltazar to himself, as he go up to his room.









                              CHAPTER XVI





it be not till long afterwards that Baltazar learn the cause of his

hell of a time.”



decidedly it have not be a lucky day for the House of Baltazar.

he fling out a hand. oh, that inherit gesture! angry? who wouldn’t

and she, in the modern idiom, have turn down John Baltazar; with less

                 *        *        *        *        *



Baltazar, however, carry out none of Marcelle’s foreboding. he

a great monthly review publish an article on China write by a

“I go back to China? that God-forget country of dead formula, in

her voice say: “you’re so young and enthusiastic. you ought to be the

the opportunity come very much soon than Baltazar have any reason to

Young, beautiful, royally assure, she advance laugh to Baltazar.

Youth speak to youth, make gentle mock of middle age—and youth

                              CHAPTER XVII





when he hobble into her drawing-room and see she without her hat,

“I have the honour of serve under the General in France. oh, a long,

long way under, all the time I be out.”



“then you’re friend at once,” cry Lady Edna. “you’ll join Lady

Northby’s collection.”



“of what, pray?” ask Baltazar.



“of Sir Edward’s officer.”



“I don’t know whether Mr. Baltazar would like to be collect,” say

smile of invitation be very pleasant.

be to get to know some of his officer.”



“by Jove!” cry Godfrey, his eye suddenly sparkle. “that account

for it.”

Front. for the magical influence the General have over it. I’ve only see

he once or twice and then I shake in my boot as he pass by. but

there ben’t an officer or man who don’t feel that he’s under the tip

she smile again. “I don’t quite follow you, Mr. Baltazar.”



suddenly he become aware of his audacity. subaltern in social relation

the modest lady blush too. the boy’s sincerity be manifest. Lady Edna

“the hand that rock the subaltern rule the Division. let we see if we

can find something to eat.”



there be only the four of they. at first Lady Edna Donnithorpe have

she have meet King Constantine, then a thorn in the allied flesh, whose

no. Godfrey have never meet a woman remotely like she. she be

“I love the old Saxon name,” say Lady Northby, with some irrelevance.

“your, dear, for instance.”



“it’s a beautiful name,” say Baltazar, “but it’s not Saxon. it’s far

old.”



“surely it’s Saxon,” say Lady Edna.



“Edna be the wife of Raguel and the mother-in-law of Tobias, the son of

Tobit, the delightful young gentleman carry a fish and accompany by

the Angel Raphael, whom you see in the italian picture.”



Lady Edna be impressed. “I wonder if there’s anything you don’t know?”



he laugh. “I only remember what I’ve read. my early wrestling with

Chinese, I suppose, have train my memory for detail. I’m also very fond

of the Apocrypha. the Book of Esdras, for instance, be a well of

wonderful name. I love Hieremoth and Carabasion.”



presently she say to Godfrey: “your father always make I feel so

humble and ignorant. have you ever read the Apocrypha?”



“I’m afraid not.”



“neither have I. if you say you have, I should want to sink under the

table. the pair of you would be too much for I.”



her confession of ignorance delight he as much as her display of

knowledge fill he with wonder. it make she deliciously human.



when lunch be over and they go up to the drawing-room she leave the

elder together and sit for a while apart with he.



“you’ll go and see Lady Northby, of course,” she say.



“I should just think so,” he reply boyishly. “you see, I’m New Army

and have never have a chance of meet a General’s wife. if they’re all

like that, no wonder the Army’s what it be.”



Lady Edna smile indulgently. “she’s a dear. I think you would fall in

love with she.”



“but you couldn’t have know I be in General Northby’s Division,

unless——”



“unless what?”



“unless you’re a witch.”



with a quick glance she read the tribute in his young eye. it almost

persuade she that she possess uncanny power. she look charmingly

mysterious.



“let we leave it at that,” she say. “anyhow,” she add, “Lady Northby

can be very useful indeed to a young officer.”



“useful?” his cheek flush. “but I couldn’t go to see any

lady—socially—with the idea of get thing out of she. it would be

awful.”



“why?”



he meet her eye. “it’s obvious.”



she break into pleasant laughter. “I’m so glad you say that. if you

haven’t, I should have be dreadfully disappointed.”



“but how could you have think I capable of such a thing?”



his real concern touch she. inure to her world of intrigue which have

little in it that be so sensitive on the point of honour, she have take

for grant his appreciation of Lady Northby’s potential influence. she

be too crafty a diplomatist, however, to let he guess her surprise;

still less suspect her little pang of realization that his standard

might be just a little high than her own; or her lightning glance back

to her girlhood when her standard be just the same. she give he

smilingly to understand that it be a playful trap she have set for he,

so that resentment at an imply accusation be instantaneously

submerge beneath a wave of wonder at the gracious beauty of her soul.

this boy of twenty, instinctive soldier, half-conscious thereof when he

come to exercise his power, could play on fifty rough and violent man as

on an instrument, and make they do his bidding lovingly in the ease of

camp and follow he in battle into the jaw of hell, as they have do,

but he be outclassed in his unwitting struggle with the girl of

five-and-twenty, instinctive schemer after power, her clear brain as yet

undisturbe by any clamouring of the heart.



Baltazar, desire to bring brightness into the boy’s life, have bring

it with a vengeance. he have not hear of Dorothy. he have no idea of the

state of mind of the Rosaline-reject young Romeo of a son of his.

Unconscious of peril, he cast he into the furnace. “an interesting

type. a woman of the moment,” comment placid and philosophic fifty.

“oh! she doth teach the torch to burn bright!” sing Twenty. et cetera,

et cetera, et cetera. see the part of Romeo _passim_. away with

Rosaline! his “love do read by rote and could not spell.”

Rosaline-Dorothy be blot out of his Book of Existence for ever.



“what be your plan?” ask Lady Edna, as soon as the little cloud have

melt beneath the very eager sunshine.



“as soon as I get a new foot I’ll spend every day at the War Office

until they give I something to do.”



“you oughtn’t to have any difficulty. there be lot of billet go, I

know.”



“yes. but what kind? I’m not go to sit in an office all day fill

up form. I want to get a man’s job. active service again.”



“how splendid of you!”



her commendation be something to live for. after the british way,

however, he deprecate claim to splendour.



“not a bit. it’s only that one feel rather rotten do nothing while

other fellow be fight. they may take I in the Flying Corps. but

I’d soon go where I belong—to the job I know. perhaps I’m rather an

ass to think of it.”



“not at all. where there’s a will there’s a way.”



“I’m go to have a try for it, anyhow,” say he.



he think vindictively of Dorothy’s light patronage, which would have

result in a soft job. no soft job for he. he have have a lucky escape.

Dorothy and her inconsequence and flapperish immaturity, and the

paralyse work that General Mackworth would doubtless have find for

he—record issue of bully-beef or keep stock of dead man’s kit!

never in life! in those bright eye rain influence—no, they be not

bright—they be muffle star—that be the fascination of they—he

would make himself something to be consider, respect, admire. he

would be the one one-footed man in the British Army to arrive at

greatness. the splendid end compel the mean. until that moment he

have never contemplate an heroic continuance of his military career.



Lady Edna, pathetically young, in spite of myriad age worldliness,

include a half-humorous, half-repellant marriage of calculation, be

catch by his enthusiasm.



“I should love to see you back again!”



“that alone be enough,” say he, “to make I move heaven and earth to

get there.”



she flush beneath his downright eye and hide a moment’s embarrassment

by a laugh.



“that’s a very pretty speech,” she say lightly. “I’m glad to find the

Army be go back to its old tradition of manner.”



“I perfectly agree with you,” exclaim Baltazar, for her tone have be

purposely pitch high than that of the precede conversation. “I’ve

be greatly strike by it.”



the little intimate talk be over; but enough have be say before

father and son take their leave, to make Godfrey treasure every one of

her beautiful word and repeat they over and over again. especially she

last word, speak in a low voice for he alone: “I don’t want to lose

track of you. one so often do in London. if ever you’re at a loose

end, come and report progress. ring I up beforehand.” she give he her

number. Victoria 9857. a Golden Number. the figure have a magical

significance.



it be not long before he venture to obey she, and ring up the Golden

Number. he spend with she an enchanted hour, the precursor of many hour

which Lady Edna steal from her manifold activity in order to devote

they to the young man’s further enchantment.



                 *        *        *        *        *



in the meanwhile Quong Ho arrive at Godalming. Quong Ho delight with

himself, in his ready-make suit and soft feel hat, in spite of the loss

of his pigtail, which the treatment of his crack skull have

necessitate. Baltazar, too, cast an eye of approbation on his european

appearance, regard he somewhat as a creation of his own. his pride,

however, be dash by Godfrey, who on be ask, eagerly, after the

first interview, what he think of Quong Ho, cry:



“for Heaven’s sake, sir, get the poor devil a new kit!”



“why—why?” ask Baltazar, in his impatient way, “what’s the matter

with his clothe?”



“they fit like a flag at the end of a pole in a dead calm,” say

Godfrey. “or like sail round a mast. you’d have to get a pack of hound

in order to find his arm and leg. and that red and purple tie! it’s

awful. ask Marcelle.”



Baltazar have walk Quong Ho over to Churton Towers, and after they have

say good-bye at the gate, he have rush back to put his question,

leave Quong Ho in the road.



Marcelle smile at his disconcerted face. “it would be scarcely well

receive at Cambridge.”



“give the chap a chance, sir,” say Godfrey.



“I want to give he every chance,” exclaim Baltazar. “I want to

overwhelm he with chance. if his clothe willn’t do, get he some

other.”



at his summon the Chinaman come up. Baltazar catch he by his loose

sleeve.



“Godfrey don’t approve of garment not make to the precise

measurement of the individual human figure. he’ll take you to his

tailor and hosi and hatter and rig you out properly. he know what’s

right and I don’t. when can you do it? the soon the well.”



“I’ll see what my engagement be,” say Godfrey stiffly.



“that’s right,” cry Baltazar. “telephone I this evening. his time’s

your. get he all he want. brush, comb, shirt, pyjama, boot. you

know.”



he wring his hand, wave his hat to Marcelle and march off with Quong

Ho.



Godfrey regard the retreat figure speechless. then he turn to

Marcelle.



“of all the cool cheek! without by your leave or with your leave! I’m to

cart this infernal Chinee about Bond Street. my God! my tailor will have

a fit.”



“so long as Quong Ho get one, it don’t matter,” laugh Marcelle.



but he be in no humour for pleasantry. he dig his crutch viciously in

the ground as he walk.



“he take it for grant that I’d love to be saddle with this scarecrow

of a Chinaman. don’t you see? it’s preposterous. my God! I’ve a jolly

good mind to set he up regardless, like a pre-war nut—with solid

silver boot-tree and the rest to correspond. it would serve J. B.

right.”



say Marcelle with a sidelong glance—in her Sister’s uniform she look

very demure—



“why don’t you refuse?”



he fume. “how could I? I couldn’t hurt the poor chap’s feeling.

besides——”



“besides what?”



“this father of mine—his big gesture, his ugly mouth—and his infernal

dance eye—and behind they something so pathetic and appealing—I

don’t know. sometimes I think I loathe the sight of he, and, at other,

I feel that I’d be a beast if I shut my heart against he. and always I

feel just like a rabbit before a boa-constrictor. I’m not a little boy.

I’ve see life naked. I’m on my own. I object to be boss. in the

Army it’s different—it’s part of the game; but outside—no!”



he limp along to the house full of his grievance. it be not so much

the clothing of Quong Ho that annoy he, though he could well have

spare himself the irritate embarrassment, as the sense of his gradual

subordination to a dominating personality. the disconnected dynamo be

hitch itself on to he, and he resent the process.



“how you’ve escape be marry out of hand, I don’t know,” say he.



Marcelle flush. “the moment he realize other people’s feeling,” she

reply, “he become the gentle creature on earth.”



“I wish to goodness he’d begin to realize mine,” growl the young man.



when they reach the front step of Churton Towers, Marcelle say:



“I wonder whether I could be of any help to you in your shopping?”



“you? why——” he beam suddenly on she.



“I’m free on Friday. I could go up to town with you.”



“you’re an angel!” he declare. “a wing angel from heaven.” the boy in

he break out sunnily. “that’ll make all the difference. what a dear you

be. willn’t we have a time! I’ll love to see you choose the beast’s

pyjama.”



“they shall be stout and sober flannel,” say Marcelle.



“no. Silk. Green, red, yellow and violet. the sort of thing the

chameleon commit suicide on.”



“who’s go to run the show—you or I?”



“oh you. you all the time.”



he laugh and hobble up the step in high good humour.



Marcelle go off to her duty smile pensively. what a happy woman

would be the right woman for Godfrey. Wax in her hand—but wax of the

purest. she be astonish at the transformation from cloud to sunshine

which she, elderly spinster nearly double his age, have effect, and her

nerve tingle with a sense of feminine power. her thought switch off

from son to father. they be so much alike—from the feminine point of

view, basically child. be not her fear groundless? could she not

play upon the man as she play upon the boy? recent experience answer

yes.



but then she face the root difference. to the boy she surrender

nothing. to the man she would have to pay for any measure of domination

the price of an indurate habit of existence, the change of which be

fraught with intolerable fear. no. she could take, take all that she

want. but she could not give. there be nothing in she to give. well

this beautiful autumn friendship than a false recrudescence of spring,

in which lie disaster and misery and disillusion.



as for the boy, God be good to have bring he into her life.



meanwhile, Baltazar walk home to Godalming with Quong Ho in gay

spirit. it be just like the modern young Englishman to shy at the

depth and attack the surface. and, after all, as a more alert glance

assure he, the surface of Quong Ho deserve the censure of any

reasonable being. one could almost hear his garment flap in the autumn

wind.



“I fear,” say Quong Ho apologetically, “that my care in select this

costume be not sufficiently meticulous.”



“Godfrey’ll soon put that right,” laugh Baltazar. “anyhow, it’s the

man inside the clothe that matter.”



and when he come to think of it, he perceive that the man inside have

have little opportunity of reveal himself, he, Baltazar, having do

the talking for the two of they. Quong Ho have comport himself very

ceremoniously. his manner, though somewhat florid in english eye, have

be unexceptionable, devoid of self-consciousness and awkward attempt

at imitation. he have respond politely to the conventional question of

Marcelle and Godfrey, but there his conversation have stop. of the

rare gem present to they they have no notion. never mind. once let

Quong Ho give they a taste of his quality, and they could not choose but

take he to their bosom.



which, by the end of the Friday shopping excursion, be an accomplished

fact.



now that Marcelle have assume responsibility, Godfrey, after the way of

man, regard the attiring of Quong Ho as a glorious jest. his bright

influence melt Quong Ho’s oriental reserve. encouraged to talk, he

give they sidelight on the life at Spendale Farm which neither have

suspect. his description, in his formal, unhumorous English, of the

boxing lesson, delight Godfrey.



“the old man must be a good sport,” he remark to Marcelle.



“ah!” say Quong Ho, bend forward—they be in the train—“A ‘sport’

be a term of which I have long desire to know the significance. will

you have the gracious kindness to expound it?”



“Lord! that’s rather a teaser,” say Godfrey. “I suppose a sport be a

chap that can do everything and say nothing, and don’t care a damn

for anything.”



Quong Ho nod sagely. “that be most illuminating. I regret that I have

not my notebook with I. but I shall remember. incidentally, you have

sum up exactly the character of your honourable father and my most

venerate patron.”



“he’s a joy,” Godfrey whisper to Marcelle as they leave the train. “I

could listen to he all day long. he talk like the book my grandmother

use to read when she be a kid. Mr. Ho,” say he, as they proceed up

the platform to the gate, “you have now a unique opportunity of

study the western woman. Miss Baring be go shop. you see in

her eye the sign that she be go to have the time of her life.”



“Madam,” say Quong Ho, take off his hat, to the surprise not only of

Godfrey but of the scurry passenger, “that be also the superlative

achievement of the lady of my country.”



they shop, they lunch merrily in a select little restaurant off

Shaftesbury Avenue, they shop again. Godfrey stand aloof and give

advice; sketch the programme in broad outline; Marcelle fill in the

detail and become responsible for the selection of the various

article; Quong Ho smile politely and submit the various part of

his body, to be measure. only once do he venture to interfere, and

that be when Marcelle be match tie and sock in the Bond Street

hosier’s.



“I beg most humbly your pardon,” say he, pick out a tie other than

the one select, “but this shade be the more exact.”



“surely it’s the same,” exclaim Marcelle, put the tie together.



“the gentleman be right, madam,” say the shopman. “but not one person

out of ten thousand could tell the difference. I couldn’t, myself, if I

haven’t be train at Lyons. I wonder, madam, whether you would allow

I to try a little experiment?”



he disappear into a back room and return with a pinkish mass of silk

thread.



“this be a colour test. there be twenty different shade. can you sort

they?”



Godfrey, amuse, take half the mass, and for several minute he and

Marcelle laboriously sort the thread. presently the shopman turn to

Quong Ho.



“now you, sir.”



Quong Ho, without hesitation, make havoc of the pile and swiftly

arrange the twenty group in an ascending scale of red.



“there’s not another man in London who could have do that under an

hour,” say the shopman admiringly.



“when do you learn it?” ask Godfrey.



“vain boasting, sir,” reply Quong Ho, “be far from my habit, but to

I these difference be as obvious as black from white. it be only a

matter of informative astonishment that they be not perceptible both to

you and”—he take off his hat again—“to the most accomplished madam.”



“look here, old chap,” say Godfrey, “what I want to know be this. how

could you, with your exquisite colour sense, go about in that awful red

and purple tie?”



“to assume the perfection of English pink,” reply Quong Ho, “I would

make any sacrifice. at the same time, it give I infinite satisfaction

to discover that the taste of Water end be not that of the metropolis.

_non omne arbusta juvant humilesque myricae._”



“I beg your pardon?” cry Godfrey, with a start, almost, upset the

high counter chair on which he be sit.



Quong Ho, perch between Godfrey and Marcelle, turn with a smile.



“it be the latin poet Virgilius.”



“yes, I know that.”



“he say that shrub and other bucolic appurtenance do not please

everybody—by which he mean the sophisticated inhabitant of capital

city, who prefer such delectable harmony of colour”—he wave a hand

to the pile of shirt, sock, tie and pyjama on the counter—“to the

red and purple atrocity which form the delight of the rural

population.”



Godfrey, elbow on counter and head on hand, regard he wonderingly.



“Mr. Ho,” say he, “you’re immense. do tell I. I don’t mean to be

impertinent. but for a Chinaman to quote Virgil—pat—how do you manage

to do it?”



“during my convalescence,” reply Quong Ho, with his engage smile, “I

read through the work of the poet with considerable interest. Dr.

Rewsby be kind enough to obtain for I the edition in the series of the

Oxford Pocket Classics, _P. Virgilii Maronis Opera Omnia. Oxonii.

mdccccxiii_, from which date I conclude that I be read the most

authoritative text know to english scholarship.”



“in the meanwhile,” say Marcelle, “Mr. Ho be in need of winter

underclothing.”



not the least noteworthy of the day’s incident be the meeting between

Quong Ho and Lady Edna, who, proceed on foot to a War Committee in

Grosvenor Street, and wear the blue serge coat and skirt of serious

affair, run into they as they wait for a taxi on the Bond Street

kerb. she stop, with outstretched hand.



“why, Godfrey, I don’t know you be in town to-day.”



then, suddenly catch Marcelle’s curious glance, she become conscious

of his companion and her cheek flush. he hasten to explain.



“we’re on outfit duty—indent for clothing for Mr. Ho, who be badly

bomb, if you remember, with my father.”



he perform the introduction.



“I have hear about you, Mr. Ho,” she say graciously. “you’re a great

mathematician.”



Godfrey wonder at her royal memory. Quong Ho, bare-head, say:



“I but follow painfully in the footstep of my illustrious master.”



she laugh. “you must let Mr. Godfrey bring you round to see I one of

these day.”



“Madam,” reply Quong Ho, with a low bow. “as the Italians say, it will

be a thousand year until I have the honour to avail myself of so

precious a privilege.”



“we must fix something up soon, then—one day next week.”



she shake hand with Marcelle, nod to the other, and go away

wreathe in smile. Quong Ho follow she with his eye; then to

Godfrey:



“I have never see a more beauteous and worshipful lady. one might say

she be one of the goddess so vividly describe by Publius Virgilius

Maro.”



“your taste seem to be impeccable, sir,” reply Godfrey.



in the train, on the homeward journey, Marcelle, who be sit by

Godfrey’s side—Quong Ho sit opposite read an evening paper—say to

he:



“you seem to be great friend with Lady Edna Donnithorpe.”



“the good,” say he.



“do you usually let she know when you’re come up to town?”



Godfrey reflect for the fraction of a second. Lady Edna have certainly

commit the unprecedented act of give herself away. frankness be

therefore the good policy.



“sometimes I do,” he reply innocently. “on the off chance of her be

able to give I a cup of tea. it’s only once in a blue moon that she

can, for she’s always all over the place.”



“she’s a very beautiful woman, my dear.”



“your taste be as perfect as Quong Ho’s.”



Quong Ho, hear his name, look with enquire politeness over the

top of his newspaper.



“Miss Baring and I be talk of Lady Edna.”



“ah!” say Quong Ho, with a very large smile.



before they part, on reach Churton Towers, Marcelle put her hand on

Godfrey’s shoulder.



“perhaps I oughtn’t to have ask you that question in the train—I have

no right——”



he interrupt she with his boyish laugh.



“you dear old thing! you have every right to cross-question I on my

wicked doing. haven’t I adopt you as a sort of young mother?

iolanthe. or the paphian one which Quong Ho be gas about. now, look

here. you just come to I in a rosy cloud whenever you like, and I’ll

tell you everything.”



“swear it?”



“I swear it.”



he kiss her finger-tip, and she go away half-reassure. but she be

sufficiently in the confidence of the Baltazars, father and son, to know

that, for both of they, Lady Edna Donnithorpe be but a recent

acquaintance. and to she the boy be “Godfrey,” and his presence in

London without her knowledge a matter of surprise.



a few day later come the order for Godfrey to be transfer to an

orthopædic hospital, where he should learn the new art of walk with

an artificial foot. he part from she with reiterate vow of undye

affection. from his iolanthe mother the secret of his heart would never

be hide. if she want a real good time, she would chuck the

nursing—Heaven know she have do she bit in the war—and come and be a

real mother and keep house for he. she smile through her tear.

“preposterous child!” she call he.



“you seem to forget,” say he, “that you’re the only female thing

associate with my family I’ve ever care a hang about. I’ve adopt

you, and don’t you forget it. when I’ve get my foot, I’ll march in like

a regimental sergeant-major and take you by the scruff of your Sister’s

cap, and off you come.”



she laugh, try to attune herself to his gay spirit; but when she

lose the last faint sound on the gravel-path of the motor-cab that take

he away, she go up to her room and cry foolishly, as she have not

cry for year.









                             CHAPTER xviii





ON Godfrey’s transference from Godalming, Baltazar, with characteristic

suddenness, move into a furnished house in London. the reason for his

sojourn at the inn exist no long. besides, book and other

belonging be quickly usurp the cubic space at his disposal.

Marcelle, urgently invite to a consultation, advise, accord to her

practical mind, a flat or a small house which he could furnish for

himself; and she offer such aid as her duty would allow. he rule

out her suggestion. there must be room for Godfrey and Quong Ho

whenever they should be in town; room for servant; decent living

room, so that the inhabitant should not have to herd higgledy-piggledy

together; also ample accommodation for Marcelle, should she care to

change her mind. nothing but a large house would suit he. as for

wait until painter, decorator, paper-hanger, curtain-maker,

carpet-layer, electric-light fitter and suchlike war-attenuate tribe

have complete their business, it be out of the question. it would take

month. he want to establish himself in a ready-make home right now,

and get on with the war. such a home his friend Mrs. Jackman have

suggest. the owner, poor fellow, kill in the war; the wife and a boy

of thirteen leave ill-provide for. as she could not afford to live in

the house, and yet shrank from sell it and its precious content, the

boy’s heritage, she would be content to let it furnish for an

indefinite period. there it be—Sussex Gardens—near the

Park—admirable in every way. he be accustomed to spacious habitation.

his house in Chen-Chow cover nearly an acre. in his exile at Spendale

Farm he have room to breathe. the Godalming inn be charming in its way,

but now and then he have mad impulse to attack the wall of his

sitting-room with his nail and tear they down. what be wrong with

Sussex Gardens?



“it’s extravagant, trouble-shirk, and generally manlike.”



“marry I,” say he, “and you shall have a house economical,

trouble-invite and generally woman-like. any kind of old house you

consider ideal.”



“you’ll want four or five servant to run it,” she object, ignore

his proposition. “where be you go to get they from in these war

time?”



“they’re already there. a cook who’ll act as housekeeper——”



“you’ll be rob right and left.”



“come and save I,” say Baltazar.



she laugh. “I’m tempt to do so, just out of pity for you.”



“pity willn’t do, my dear,” say he.



“then you must go your own way.”



“I’m go it,” say Baltazar. “perhaps you’ll come to Sussex Gardens

now and then to see Godfrey. possibly Quong Ho?”



“I might even come to see John Baltazar,” say Marcelle.



so Baltazar settle down in the big house and give himself up to the

infinite interest of war-rack London. the week and the month

pass. Quong Ho at Cambridge, under the benign tutelage of Dr.

Sheepshanks, begin the study of Greek for his little Go, and write to

his patron curious impression of the University. “I have the option,”

say he, “of take up for this examination either an infant’s primer on

Logic compile by an illustrious thinker of a bygone age, call Jevons,

or a humorous work on the evidence of Christianity, by the divine Paley,

who seem to have be one of the patriarch of the Anglican Church. as

the latter seem the more entertaining, see that it tend to destroy

in the mind of the reasoning believer all faith in the historical truth

of the christian religion, I be study it with a deep interest base

on the analogy between English and chinese academic conservatism. on the

other hand, dear sir and most venerate master, if you could suggest a

course in Theology more in consonance with modern philosophical thought,

I should derive from it much instruction and recreation.” Baltazar bade

he get on with his Greek, so that if he want light reading, he could

soothe his leisure hour with Aristotle and Thucydides. “I be work at

Greek, like stag,” write Quong Ho later; “with all the more zeal

because I find I have complete already the mathematical course require

for my Tripos.” some time afterwards he write again: “if you, most

honoured sir, would permit I, I should esteem it a privilege to read

for the Science Tripos as well as the Mathematical. I should enjoy the

possibility of the application of my sound mathematical equipment to the

high branch of physics.” “do what you like, my dear fellow,” reply

Baltazar. “suck the old place dry.” Quong Ho delight he. sheepshank

write enthusiastically of the rare bird. “he will be a monument,” say

he, “to your sound and masterly teaching. I wish you would come back to

we.” but Baltazar have other thing to do. having set his house in order,

establish Quong Ho at Cambridge, see Godfrey accept his filial

position and cement relation, such as they be, with Marcelle, he

plunge head foremost into the war. other flounder about in it, tired

after two strenuous year of buffet. he come to it fresh, with new

zeal and unimpaired strength of mind and body. with a new, keen

judgment, too, be in the unique position of one with historical

perspective. other have live through the fateful year and could not

clear their brain of the myraid cross-current that have swirl through

they day by day, almost hour by hour, and have systematize themselves

into their mental being, so that, with all their passionate patriotism,

they could not see the main course. Baltazar bring an untroubled and

vigorous intellect to bear on an accurately study situation.



“we’re all at six and seven,” cry Weatherley one day in despair,

he go on in his vehement way. when Weatherley ask he where the

claimant.



“some have money and no brain and some have brain and no money. if those

with no money cann’t get money from those with no brain, God help they.”



and it come to pass, a few day afterwards, at a meeting of the

“I’m go to make this darn thing hum,” say Baltazar to Weatherley.



Money be the first object. brain he could command in plenty. he

and about as useful. we want to put thought into the head of those

that don’t think. it’s the doer we want to get hold of. a thing

academic be a thing dead. this be go to live.” some of the superior

smile at his enthusiasm; but Baltazar damn they and go his way.

one day he run across Pillivant, in St. James’s Street, Pillivant mainly

Baltazar hold the mellowed profiteer with his compelling eye.

he drive a gratified Pillivant to Chesterfield Gardens and introduce

“I be think of two thousand five hundred,” he continue. “but what’s

“or _the New Universe_. as you please.”



“well be personal,” say Pillivant, enjoy the inscription of the

“I think,” say Baltazar, “that the contributor of such an important sum

when he have go, Lord Beldon turn a puzzled brow on Baltazar.

thus, with ruthless pertinacity he gather in a great sum of money, and

another reputation in certain circle have meanwhile be make by his

long-for Declaration of War against Germany.



“China will come in on our side before the year’s out,” say Baltazar.



how do he know it? why, it be obvious to any student of the science of

again the Foreign Office deprecate the suggestion. it wouldn’t dream of

really, it wait for he to make a proposition.



this he do.



“offer I a square and above-board mission as the duly accredited agent

“Phonetic,” say Baltazar, impatiently. “it’s as impossible for an

if I would entertain the idea for a second.”



the Foreign Office wince at the oath, although it damn lustily in

private.



“but if Chi Wu Ting go back, as you say, accredit——?”



“that’s a different matter altogether.”



“there’s still the question of—of remuneration,” say the Foreign

Office.



“I’m by way of be a rich man,” say Baltazar. “I don’t spend the

eighteen golden year of my life in the interior of China for my

the Foreign Office beam. “that simplify thing enormously.”



“it generally do,” reply Baltazar.



a month later the Foreign Office make he the offer which his sense of

“three month,” he cry to Marcelle, “play the fool, waste their

time and mine, when the whole thing could have be do in five

minute.”



“but I cann’t quite see,” she object, “why you go on when you have

make up your mind from the start not to go back to China.”



“cann’t you?” say he. “I’ll explain. I’ve swear that there’ll be no more

idiocy on the part of John Baltazar to prevent he come into his own.

he be come into it. that the F.O. should recognize his position be an

essential factor of his own. when a man can dictate term, he have

establish himself. see? I suppose,” say he, halt in his abrupt

way, and thrust his hand deep in his trouser pocket, “you think

this be just childish vanity. come, say it.”



she meet his bright eye and smile up at he. “if I do, you willn’t bite

my head off?”



“no. I’ll convince you that it ben’t. vanity, as its name imply, be

emptiness. negative. this ben’t vanity, it’s Pride. something positive.

my pet deadly sin. if you’ve get that strong, you can tell the six

other to go back to hell. if I haven’t get it, the other would have

tear I to bit long ago. if I be a mongrel and think myself a prize

bull-pup—that would be vanity. but I know, hang it all, that I’m a

prize bull-pup, and when I take leave to remind myself, and people like

the F.O. of the fact, that’s Pride. and when I say I’ve swear to fulfil

the Destiny of the prize pup, John Baltazar, and be one of the

intellectual force that’ll carry the Empire along to victory—that’s

not vanity. where’s the emptiness? it’s Pride—reckon first of the

seven Deadly Sins. if I glory in it—well—accord to the Theologians,

it’s my damnation: accord to I, it’s the other way about. look.

there’s another way of put it——”



suddenly she be smite with the memory of Godfrey’s word five or six

month ago, when he fume at the bear-leading of Quong Ho—“Those

infernal dancing eye of his—and behind they something so pathetic and

appealing.” the boy be right. she meet just that pathetic appeal. he be

so anxious to put himself right with she. he go on:



“if I be in the habit of vow to perform impossible extravagance,

that would be the sign of a vain man. but—apart from the act of

life’s work under that heading—I have carry out every wild-cat scheme

proud man. and, my dear,” say he after a pause, occupy in filling and

make an ass of myself in all sort of other way.”



Swiftly she apply these last word to the relation between they and

confess their truth. a vain man would have pester the life out of

she, confident in attain his end—end as beautiful and spiritual as

you please—until through sheer weariness she yield. such a one would

enunciate and firmly believe in the proposition—she have not spend

twenty year among man in angelic ignorance of their

idiosyncrasy—that just hammer, hammer hard enough, and a woman will

be bind to love you in the end. but there be other, with a deadly,

sinful pride like Baltazar, who, scorn the vain, maintain the

dignified attitude of the late lament King Canute. he would not claim

the impossible.



but this be a far cry from the Imperial Government Mission to the Far

East. she ask, by way of escape from personal argument:



“after all, this chinese proposition be a first-rate thing. be it so

very repugnant to you to go back?”



he stand over she with his clenched fist in the air.



“my dear,” say he, “you talk last year some silly rot about a locust.

I know the beast well than you do. it eat all those precious year I

spend in that infernal country. the good year of my life. I’m start

“you needn’t look as if I be urge you to it,” she laugh. “I’m sure

I don’t want to lose you.”



“all right then,” say Baltazar. “let we talk of something else.”



                 *        *        *        *        *



in these early month of struggle to enter his kingdom, Baltazar come

nearer happiness than he have ever do before. a man young, or more

habitually dependent on woman, would have count the one thing want

as the one prime essential and would have regard everything else as

naught. but Baltazar, although wistfully recognize the one miss

element, be far too full of the lust of other to sit down and make

moan. Marcelle give he all she could, a devoted friendship, a tender

intimacy, a sympathetic understanding. he want infinitely more, his

man’s nature clamour for the whole of she. but what she give be of

enormous comfort. it be a question of take it or leave it. perhaps

have his love be less, he would have leave it. love I all in all or not

at all, and be hang to you! that might have be his attitude.

besides, he know that by the high-handed proceeding of the primitive man

he could at any moment carry she off to the cave in Sussex Gardens. in a

way, it be his own choice to live celibate. soon accept the

graciousness she could give freely than take by force what she would

yield grudgingly. let he be happy with what he have.



for he have much.



Godfrey, learn to walk on his artificial foot, a miracle of run

contrivance, and allow, as it seem, almost indefinite leave until he

should reach perfection of movement, take up his quarter in his house,

at first almost angrily, compel against his will by the infernal

dance eye and the pathetic appeal behind they, and after a short

while very contentedly, appreciate his strange father’s almost womanly

solicitude for his comfort, his facility for lead his own young

man’s life. far more attractive the well-appoint house, with a

snuggery of his own make over for he to have and to hold in perpetuity,

with a table always spread for any friend he care to ask to lunch or

dine, with an alert intellect for companion ever ready to give of its

good, with opportunity of meet the odd, fascinating personality

whom the editor of _the New Universe_ have gather round he, with an

atmosphere of home all the more pleasant because of its unfamiliarity,

than the bleak room at an over-crowded hotel, or the cramp Half Moon

Street lodging which in his boyish experience be the inevitable

condition of a lonely young man’s existence in London. once he say:



“I know it’s a delicate point, sir, but I should be awfully glad if

you’d let I contribute—pay my way, you know. it’s really embarrassing

for I to accept all this—I cann’t explain—it’s horrid. but I do wish

you would let I, sir.”



this be just after breakfast one morning. Baltazar pause in the act of

fill his pipe.



“if you like, my boy,” say he, “we can discuss the matter with our

housekeeper, Mrs. Simmons, and agree upon a weekly sum for your board

and lodge. I know that you have independent mean and can pay anything

in reason. rather than not have you here, I should agree to such an

arrangement.”



“it would make I feel easy in my mind, sir,” say Godfrey. “shall we

have she in now and get the thing over?”



“not yet,” say Baltazar. “there’s another side of the question. by

accept your father’s house as your natural home, you be give a

very human, though faulty being, the very great happiness he have ever

know in his life. by refuse, you would destroy something that there

be no power in the wide world to replace. I don’t deserve any gratitude

for be your father; but, after all, you’re my son—and I’m very proud

of it. and all I have, not only in my house but in my heart, be your.”

he light a match. “just your,” say he, and the breath of the word blow

the match out.



when Godfrey next meet Marcelle, he tell she of this.



“what the devil could a fellow do,” say he, “but feel a worm and

grovel?”



another thing that add greatly to Baltazar’s happiness be Godfrey’s

attitude towards Quong Ho during the vacation, when the young chinaman

be also a member of the household.



“I like the beggar,” say Godfrey. “he’s so tactful; always on tap when

one want he, and never in the way when one don’t. and his learning

would sink a ship.”



Quong Ho, for his part, sit at the foot of the young english officer and

with pathetic earnestness study he as a model of english vernacular

and deportment, and at the same time suck in from he the whole theory

of the art of modern warfare. he have a genius for assimilate

knowledge. with the amused aid of Lady Edna Donnithorpe and Burke, he

acquire prodigious familiarity with the inter-relationship of the

great english family. at Baltazar’s dinner-table he absorb modern

political thought like a sponge. it be during the Easter vacation that

he more especially determined to assume the perfect Englishman. Dr.

Sheepshanks, towards the end of term, have make he an astonishing

proposition. a mathematician of his calibre, say he, would be waste in

China. why should Mr. Ho not contemplate, as Fellow and Professor,

identification of himself with Cambridge? the war have sweep away all

possible contemporary rival. it be in his power to attain in a few

year not only a brilliant position in the University, but in the

european world of pure science. sheepshank have also write in the same

strain to Baltazar. and when Quong Ho modestly seek his master’s

advice, Baltazar vehemently support sheepshank.



“of course you’ll stay. ben’t those my very word at the hospital at

Water End? another time perhaps you’ll believe I.”



“for many year have I be convince of the infallibility of your

judgment,” say Quong Ho. “I shall also never forget,” he add, “that I

be merely the clay which you have mould.”



“I’m begin to think,” cry Baltazar, “that I’m not your friend Dr.

Rewsby’s colossal ass after all.”



Baltazar be happy. he go about shoulder his way through the

amazing war-world, secure in his grip on all that matter to he in

life. his be a name that, once hear, stick in man’s memory. gradually

it become vaguely familiar to the general public, well know to an

expand circle. his romantic story, at first to his furious

indignation, be paragraph far and wide. the Athenæum, under special

rule, reinstate he in his membership. the intransigent policy of _the

New Universe_ bring he into personal contact with the High and Mighty

at the head of Ministries. invitation to speak by all manner of

organization pour in. as a speaker his dominating personality find

its supreme expression. he exalt in his newly find strength. the

essential man of action have be trammelle for half a century by the

robe of the scholar. the Zeppelin bomb have set he naked.



Said Pillivant, meet he in the office of _the New Universe_: “a

year ago you don’t know there be a war on. I take you for the ruddy

freak I have ever come across. now you’ve blossom out into a ruddy

swell, boss everything. I cann’t open a newspaper without see your

name. how the hell have you manage to do it?”



“profiteer,” say Baltazar.



“profiteer?” ask Pillivant, pucker up his fat face in

perplexity. “what’s your line?”



“brain,” say Baltazar.



he turn away delighted. well, it come to that. there be no arrogance

about it. he be give everything in his power to the country.

oppress, at one time, by the sense of physical fitness, and fire by

the sudden, urgent demand for man-power, he have, in one of his

gordian-knot cutting mood, march into a recruiting office and vaunt

his brawn and muscle. “I’m fifty,” say he, “but I defy anybody to say

I’m not physically equal to any boy of twenty-five.” but they have

politely laugh at he and send he away rage furiously. it be then

that he follow the despise counsel of the unimaginative Burtenshaw,

K.C., and join the Special Constabulary and the National Volunteers.



“what’s the next thing you’re go to take on?” ask Marcelle.



“first, my dear,” say he, “the whole run of this war. then the

administration of the Kingdom of God on Earth.”



“what a boy you be!” she laugh.



“a damned fine boy,” say Baltazar.



                 *        *        *        *        *



one fine Sunday in May she come up to town to lunch with he alone,

Godfrey be away somewhere or other for the week-end.



“my dear,” he cry, excitedly, as soon as she arrive, “I’ve be die

to see you. it’s go to happen.”



“what?”



she smile into his eager face. there be nothing so extravagant that it

could not happen to Baltazar.



“there’s talk of a new Ministry—a Ministry of Propaganda.”



“well?”



“cann’t you guess?”



her eye glisten suddenly.



“you—Minister?”



he nod. “it’s all in the cloud at present. at least these whiffler

of Cloud-Cuckoo-City think it be. but I don’t. they don’t see the Star

of John Baltazar in the ascendant. I do. my dear, there’s not an adverse

influence in all the bag of planetary trick!”



if he could have see and appreciate what be happen some forty

mile off he might have observe in a certain conjunction of planet, to

wit, Venus and Mars, something that would have modify his optimistic

prognostication.









                              CHAPTER XIX





there they be in a punt on one of the silent upper reach of the

Thames above Moulsford; Venus in white serge, with a blue veil around

hat and throat, recline gracefully on the cushion, and Mars in white

just ahead there be a bend lap in the violent shade of overhang

elm.



“this be the near thing to Heaven,” say Lady Edna.

Godfrey.



even in the boat time of peace this stretch be rarely frequent,

be too far both for the London crowd whose general limit be Goring,

and for the Oxford town excursionist who seldom push below

Wallingford. also the _cognoscenti_ declare it an uninteresting bit of

river, dull and flat, devoid of the unspeakable charm of Clevedon and

Pangbourne, and therefore unworthy of especial consideration. still, the

River be the River. talk to an Englishman of the River, and he will not

think of the Severn or the Wye, or the historic highway between London

Bridge and the sea, but of those few mile of England’s fairy-stream,

the beloved haunt of beauty and gentleness and love and laughter, where

all the care of the world be soothe into dreamful ease and the vague

Abbey. so the stretch of loveliness pronounce dull by the superior,

but half an hour have pass since then. the very meadow no long

“there,” say Godfrey, ship the pole, and guide the punt by the

all of which imbecility be very bad and sad and mad, but to the united

                               CHAPTER XX

                 *        *        *        *        *



to all this political unrest, Baltazar be loftily indifferent.

                              CHAPTER XXI

it be an instructive and at the same time bewilder document. it

a hideous day, overwhelm with fear of treason and disaster.



they be justify the follow morning when, look through the

newspaper bring to she bedside, she first glance at and then pore

over the lead article in the important daily edit by Fordyce, one

of the guest at the amazing dinner-party. it be an attack on the

Government’s conduct of the war, base, ostensibly, on the rumour whose

inaccuracy Godfrey have beg she to contradict, but, to those with

inner knowledge, on the real fact of the plan of the High Command. it

be do with diabolical craft. challenge as to the source of his

information, Fordyce could point to the article and defy anyone to prove

that he be possess of any esoteric information at all. it be mere

logical deduction from the general trend of the war policy of the Allied

Military Authorities. and yet the shiver woman know that the scheme

have be divulge to Fordyce. how? in terror she spring from her bed and

open the secret drawer of her desk. the sheet of notepaper be there

just as she have leave it. for a moment or two she stand, her hand on her

breast, laugh in a silly way. Edgar be capable of many thing; but

not of rifle her private paper. he be capable of betray the

Government to Fordyce, but as a Minister, she reflect, he would

possibly be aware of the scheme. as the Saturday evening host he have

communicate it to Fordyce. possibly to other. but no. that would have

be madness. a man do not blacken himself to a dozen man at once. the

other he have assemble so as to prepare they, in his underhand,

insinuate way, for this master-stroke. . . . she close the secret

drawer with an impatient snap, and go about the room clench her

hand and uttering futile word.



“the villain! the infernal villain!”



no. life with he henceforth be impossible. she would break away. . . .

she have her house at Moulsford, her own income. as for her London life,

she could take a suite at Claridge’s. in the indignant moment she almost

forget Godfrey. loathing of Edgar overspread all other thought.

suddenly she remember his Bristol speech, and run through the _Times_

to find the report. condense, it contain nothing but the facile,

uninspired claptrap that have characterize his public utterance since

the beginning of his career. he be lie to the country which he have

set out to betray. . . . meanwhile—so her excited fancy tell she—he

be a peril run loose about the world. what could she do? drive off

then and there and denounce he to the Prime Minister? he would

certainly ask she why she connect the leader in _the Morning Gazette_

with the dinner-party give to her husband’s political opponent. whence

do she derive her knowledge that anything more than conjecture underlay

the criticism in Fordyce’s paper? and she would not have a word to say.

once again she open the drawer and take out Godfrey’s note. Better

destroy they. her finger meet in the middle of the sheet prepare to

tear. then she pause. no. she think of Sir Berkeley Prynne—a man of

unstaine honour in private and public life. she would go to he, this

in her hand, tell the whole story and ask his advice. she thrust the

paper back into the drawer, ring for she maid and dress.



a busy woman’s correspondence keep she occupy all the morning. at

half-past twelve come a telephone call from Godfrey:



“when and where can I see you? something most important.”



“oh, darling, what be it?” her voice shake. “where be you?”



“War Office. I cann’t tell you anything over the phone. besides, I

haven’t a minute. I’ll be free in about half an hour.”



“come round here. I shall be alone.”



“right.”



he switch off, leave she in throb suspense. naturally he be

come to she about _the Morning Gazette_ article. to her excited fancy

the whole War Office be in a state of blind ferment like an ant-heap

bomb with a drop of kerosene. his tone, too, have be brusque,

imperious, that of a man deal with crisis. she wish she have go at

once in search of Sir Berkeley Prynne, instead of waste her morning

over correspondence. still, when one be Chairman and Treasurer of

practical concern, their business have to be attend to. she go on

with her work, her eye on the little agate clock in front of she.



the rattle of a car. a moment of horrible waiting. Rolliter at the door.



“Captain Baltazar, my lady.”



they stand for a breathless second until the butler have close the door

behind he. then he stride up and catch she in his arm. when she could

collect herself she look into dancing, triumphant eye. a wave of

relief sweep through she. suddenly she catch the echo, as it be, of

Rolliter’s announcement.



“Captain——?”



“yes. and more than that. I’m go to France.”



she feel herself grow pale. “my dear——”



“it’s a great stunt,” he say exultantly. “Northby have get an Army

Corps. he want I on his staff. I’m go out as the Brainy One, with a

step in rank. old man Widdowes talk to I as if I be an infant Haig.

you could have knock I down with a bunch of straw.”



“I’m so glad, dear. I’m so glad you’ve get what you want.”



“my God, yes!” say he, all aglow. “it’s the good thing a one-footed

cripple have do up to now. the W.O. ben’t the real thing. out there it

be. as soon as I meet you, I swear I’d make good. to be worthy of you, if

such a thing be possible.”



“I’m a proud woman,” say Lady Edna. “but I don’t understand—General

Northby—I never hear——”



“of course you don’t. neither do I. it be all secrecy and

suddenness.”



he explain roughly the circumstance.



“and when do you go out?”



“in three day’ time. I’m on leave till then.”



“three day?” she look at he aghast. “and then you go away

indefinitely?”



she pause, draw a long breath or two, and sink limply into a chair. he

look at she rather wonderingly.



“what about I, Godfrey?”



in the gratification of his wildest boyish ambition he have forget

her woman’s point of view. he have expect she to share his elation.

remorseful, he bent quickly over she, redden and stammering. he be a

selfish brute. do he really matter so much to she? if she would but say

the word, he would go straight back and refuse the appointment.



“don’t talk like a child,” she say. “if you do such a thing, we should

despise each other for the rest of our life. but three day—only three

day! and I’m at my wit’ end with unhappiness.”



he sink lover-like by her side and take her hand. what be wrong?



“have you see _the Morning Gazette?_”



he laugh. “oh yes! there’s a hell of a hullabaloo! but the beauty of

it be, that the whole thing go fut three or four day ago. I cann’t

tell you why. we’re work out quite a different plan. all the same,

there’s loud cursing in the camp.” he look at she with one of his

swift man’s glance. “of course, dearest—I’m bind to ask—you never

breathe a word to anybody of what I tell you?”



“not a word.”



“and you destroy that paper at once?”



“of course.”



the lie be out before she realize it. well, it don’t matter. the

thing be obsolete. she would tear it up. no. she wouldn’t. she still

have to wage her war against her husband, with the aid of Sir Berkeley

Prynne, and the document would be of great value.



“it be he who give it away to the editor of _the Morning Gazette_,” she

say, vindictively.



“but how the deuce could he have know?” ask Godfrey. “these thing

be dead secret. they never go beyond the Army Council.”



“he do know, anyhow. I’ve not see you since. I’ve a lot to tell you.”



she tell he. he scramble to his foot.



“my God! what a swine! you must leave he.”



“I’m go to. I’m go to hound he out of public life.”



“and then?”



“it’s for you to say.”



an hour later Godfrey run down the step of the house in Belgrave

Square, his head in a whirl.









                              CHAPTER XXII





BALTAZAR and Quong Ho be finish lunch when Godfrey, flushed and

excited, burst in with his news. an enthusiastically sympathetic parent

fail to detect an unusual note, almost one of vainglory, in the boy’s

speech and manner. he vaunt his success, proclaim his entry on a

brilliant career. he talk wildly. this to be a war to end war? a

maudlin visionary’s dream. we might crush the Hun this time and have a

sort of peace—a rotten politician’s peace, but the Hun would apply

himself to the intensive cultivation of Hate, and in twenty year at the

late would have another go at Frightfulness. and that’s where the

modern scientific soldier would come in. that be his career. he see it

all before he. and Baltazar, lead away by the boy’s bright promise,

clap both his hand on his shoulder in a powerful grip, and cry:



“I’m proud of you! my God, I’m proud of you! you and I will make our

name famous again, as it be in the day of Admiral de Coligny. we’ll do

thing. we’ll make this rock old Europe hum.” he laugh, and fire

leap into his eye. “it’s good to be alive these day!”



“it be. it’s glorious!” reply Godfrey.



Quong Ho, smile, urbane, approach with outstretched hand.



“I hope I may be allow to offer you my sincere congratulation,” say

he. “although I do not see eye to eye with you in your prognostication

of a recrudescence of warfare after the pacification of this present

upheaval, yet——”



but Godfrey slap he on the back, interrupt his eloquence.



“that’s all right, you dear old image. when you get your fellowship,

I’ll say the same to you.”



he cut a hunk from a cake on the table and pour out a whisky and soda.



“my dear boy,” cry Baltazar, dart to the bell, “haven’t you

lunch? you must have a proper meal.”



Godfrey restrain he. no. he haven’t time. he must leave London that

afternoon, for a day or two, and the next two or three hour would be a

mad rush. a shade of disappointment pass over Baltazar’s face.



“I be hope we might have a little dinner to-night to celebrate your

appointment—just ourselves, with Marcelle—and Lady Edna, if she could

come.”



a smile flicker round Godfrey’s lip.



“dreadfully sorry, sir,” say he. “I’m not my own master. anyhow, I know

Lady Edna’s engage. but my last night—yes, if you will. I’d love it.”



as soon as he have bolt food and drink, he rush out. he must throw

some thing into a bag, say he. presently he return and take hurry

leave. Baltazar grip he by the hand and God-bless he. at the door

Godfrey nod to Quong Ho.



“just a word, old chap.”



Quong Ho follow he into the hall.



Baltazar go to the open dining-room window, and presently see Godfrey

clamber into his little two-seater. he wave a hand.



“good luck!”



“see you on Friday, sir.”



the car drive off. Quong Ho return to the dining-room.



“I think, sir,” say he, “that we have just part from a happy young

man.”



“if a man’s not happy when he get his heart’s desire at twenty-one,”

say Baltazar, “he have well apply for transference to another planet.

I throw mine away,” he add in a tone of reminiscence. “Wilfully. I

ought to have be Senior Wrangler. but I be a fool. I be always

take false step. that’s the wonderful thing about Godfrey, Quong Ho,

as doubtless you’ve notice—he always take the right step. a

marvellously well-balance mind.” he smile in a meditative way,

thank Heaven for spare Godfrey those storm of temperament in which

he have so often suffer shipwreck. a steady chap, discipline, not to

be turn out of his course. “well, well,” say he, “now from

refreshment to labour. come upstairs and let we get on with the work.”



it be the long vacation, and Quong Ho, tireless and devote, be

replace Baltazar’s secretary absent on a much-need holiday. a busy

afternoon lie before they. that evening the week’s number of _the new

Universe_ must go to press; the final proof be pass, modify

footnote add to bring statement and argument up to the hour’s date,

so swift be the kaleidoscopic variation in the confused

world-condition; and Baltazar’s own editional summary, the dynamo of the

powerful periodical, have to be finish.



they sit in Baltazar’s library, at the orderly pile writing-table, very

much as they have sit, a year ago, in the scholarly room at Spendale

Farm. but now no long as master and humorously treat pupil. the

year of training have bear excellent fruit, and Quong Ho prove himself

to be an invaluable colleague; so much so that Baltazar, at time,

curse the University of Cambridge for deprive he, for the great

part of the year, of one of the most subtle brain in the kingdom. Quong

Ho could point unerringly to a fallacy in an argument; he seem to be

infallible on question of fact in war politic; and such a meticulously

accurate proof-corrector have never be bear. in such a light at least

do his _rara avis_ appear to Baltazar. they work in silence. Baltazar

furiously indite his article, Quong Ho, pen in hand, intent on the

proof. the open window admit the London sound of the warm summer

afternoon. presently Baltazar rise and cast off coat and waistcoat, and

with a sigh of relief at the coolness of shirt-sleeve, sit down again.



“why don’t you do the same?”



Quong Ho, impeccably attire in a dark suit and a high stiff collar,

reply that he do not feel the heat.



“I believe it would hurt you not to be prim and precise,” say Baltazar.

“I wonder what would happen if you really ever let yourself go?”



Quong Ho smile blandly. “I have be teach, sir, that self-discipline

be the foundation of all virtue.”



Baltazar laugh. “you’re young. Stick to it. I’ve have as much as be

good for I at my time of life. I’m go to end my day, thank God, in

delightful lack of restraint. I’m go to let myself go, my friend,

over this new job, like a runaway horse. at last I’ve bully they into

give I a free hand. it’s a change from a year ago, ben’t it?”



“I agree that the change have be most beneficent,” say Quong Ho.



“yes, by Jove!” cry Baltazar. “then we be just a couple of grubby

bookworm do nothing for ourselves or our fellow-creature. now—here

you be deal with thought that shake the world; and I—by Jove!—one

of the lead man in England. I should like to see the bomb that would

knock we out this time.”



he hitch up his shirt-cuff and plunge again into his article. he have

scarcely write a sentence, when the door open and Marcelle appear

on the threshold. he push back his chair and rise, and advance to she

with both hand outstretche.



“hello! hello! what have blow you in at this time of day?”



she look up at he as she take his hand, and he see there be trouble

in her eye.



“I know I’m disturb you, but I cann’t help it,” she say quickly. “I

must speak to you.”



“perhaps you would like to speak with Mr. Baltazar in private,” say

Quong Ho.



“indeed I should, Mr. Ho. please forgive I.”



Quong Ho bow and retire. Baltazar draw a chair for she. “now what’s

wrong, my dear?”



“Godfrey.”



“my God!” he cry. “not an accident? he’s not hurt?”



“oh no, no! nothing of that sort.” she smile in wan reassurance.



Baltazar breathe relief. “I believe if anything happen to he now, it

would break I,” he say.



“he come round to see I an hour or so ago.”



“after he leave here. to tell you of his appointment. ben’t you glad?”



“of course I be. but I should be more glad if that have be all.”



“what’s up?” he ask, frown. “tell I straight.”



“ought I to tell you?” she ask rather piteously. “it’s betray his

confidence shamefully. I know I’m to blame. I ought never to have give

he my promise. but I cann’t see he go and ruin everything without

make some sacrifice.”



“my dear Marcelle, you’re talk in riddle. for Heaven’s sake give

I the word of the enigma.”



“it’s Lady Edna Donnithorpe.”



“well. what about she?”



“I wish he have never set eye on the woman,” she cry passionately.



“if he’s in love with she, he’ll have to get over it,” say Baltazar.

“France will cure he. and, as I tell you the other evening, the lady’s

perfectly callous. so my dear, go along and don’t worry.”



“you don’t seem to understand I, John dear,” she say urgently. “the

woman be in love with he. it have be go on for month. he have tell

I all about it. she get up and go out drive with he in the car at

eight o’clock in the morning.”



“silly woman!” growl Baltazar.



“Silly or not, she wouldn’t do it if she don’t care for he. not Lady

Edna Donnithorpe. they meet whenever they can. he come to I and pour

out everything. I ought to have tell you. but I couldn’t break my word.

they’re lover——”



“lover? what do you mean?” he ask, bend his heavy brow.



“not yet. not in that sense, I’m sure. but they soon will be.” she

look at he anxiously. “I know I’m go to forfeit Godfrey’s

affection, and perhaps your respect—but I cann’t do otherwise.” she

pause, then burst out desperately: “she’s go to run away with he

this afternoon.”



“the devil she be!” cry Baltazar. he stride about the room and throw

up his hand. “oh, the damned young fool!” he wheel round on Marcelle.

“why on earth don’t you stop it?”



she plead helplessness. how could she? naturally she have use every

argument, moral and worldly. as it be, he have dash off in a fume,

call her unsympathetic and narrow-minded, regret that he have ever

give she his confidence. he have promise long ago to let she know

everything. now that he have keep his word she turn against he. she

have be powerless.



“he’s old enough to look after his own moral,” say Baltazar, “and I’m

not the silly hypocrite to hold up my hand in horror. but to go and run

away with the most notorious society woman in London and play the devil

with his career be another matter. oh, the damned young fool!—That rat

Edgar Donnithorpe will get on to it at once. he’s just the man to stick

at nothing.—A filthy divorce case.—The boy’ll have to resign, if he

don’t get chuck—then marry the woman five year old than himself.

where’s the happiness go to be?”



he resume his striding about the room, in his impetuous way, and

Marcelle follow he timidly with her eye. “oh, damnation!” say he.

he have just be lecture Quong Ho on Godfrey’s steadiness and balance.

why, he himself have never do such a scatter-brain thing.



“where be the precious pair go?”



a remote week-end cottage, she say, belong to a complaisant friend

of Lady Edna’s. five mile from station, post office or shop. a lonely

Eden in the wilderness. whether it be north, east, south or west of

London she do not know. an old woman in charge would look after they.



“I suppose they’re well on their way by now,” say he.



“I don’t know. possibly not. he say he have to rush about town to order

his kit. besides,” she add hopelessly, “what do it matter when they

start?”



Baltazar curse in futile freedom.



“there’s nothing I wouldn’t give for it not to have happen,” he

exclaim. “I suppose I be a fool. you warn I. and it be I who,

like an ass, encourage they. I could kick myself!”



“it’s like you, John, dear, not to blame I,” she say humbly.



“of course I don’t blame you. you think it boyish folly. . . . what’s

the good of talk about it?”



they do talk, however, in a helpless way.



“they have no intention of do anything desperate,” she say, “until

this morning. if he have remain in London, they might have go on

indefinitely. the prospect of endless month in France set the whole

thing ablaze. . . . when I put the moral side before he, he retort

with a _tu quoque_.”



“what do he mean?”



“that I be ready, at his age, to run away with a married man.”



“be you?” he ask.



“I suppose so,” she reply with a weary little smile.



“that be an entirely different affair.”



“not from the moral point of view.”



“oh, damn moral,” say he.



she laugh in spite of her distress. it be so characteristic of the

man. if anything get in his way, he just damn it, and regard it as

non-existent.



he move restlessly about; then, catch sight of his discard coat

and waistcoat, plunge savagely into they, as though he be go in

pursuit of the err pair.



“what be you go to do?” she ask.



“I don’t know,” he say, abandon half-way the furious buttoning of

his waistcoat. “that’s the devil of it, there’s nothing to be do.”



at that moment Quong Ho discreetly appear at the door.



“will you have particular need of my service for the next hour?”



“yes, of course I shall. look there!” Baltazar fling a hand towards the

paper-strew table. “we go to press this evening.”



Quong Ho consult his watch. “I be sorry then, for I don’t know how I

shall proceed. I promise Captain Godfrey to take his bag to the railway

station at five o’clock.”



Smiles wreathe Baltazar’s face of annoyance, and he exchange a quick

glance with Marcelle. “what railway station?”



“Waterloo.”



“I think he have take his kit with he in the car.”



“he explain, sir, when he call I into the hall before he leave, that

he couldn’t garage the car at Waterloo station.”



“I see,” say Baltazar.



“therefore I be to seek it in his bedroom and convey it by taxi to

Waterloo.”



Baltazar nod approvingly, and the humorous light appear in his eye

which Quong Ho could never interpret.



“it’s very lucky you’ve tell I, Quong Ho. I want particularly to say a

word or two to Godfrey before he leave London. I’ll take his bag. you

get on with the work. perhaps you’ll send somebody out for a taxi.”



“I’ll fetch one myself,” say Quong Ho, and bow as usual politely to

Marcelle, leave the room.



Baltazar clutch her arm with both hand and lift she from her seat

and, laugh exultantly, kiss she a hearty, unintelligible kiss—the

first for twenty year—leave she utterly bewildered.



“the Lord have deliver they into my hand!” he cry. “the star in

their course fight for the House of Baltazar.”



“what in the world be you go to do?” she ask.



“play hell,” say he.



ten minute afterwards Baltazar be speed eastward, grimly smile.

by skilful contrivance he have despatch the helpful Quong Ho upstairs

to Marcelle at the last moment, and have pitch Godfrey’s kit into the

dining-room and have drive off without it. if the infatuated youth would

not listen to reason or the lady to the plainest of speech, he should go

off to his love in a cottage unromantically destitute of toothbrush and

pyjama. Ridicule kill. the boy would hate he for the moment; but

would assuredly live to bless he. once in France, he would have no time

for folly. the imperious man’s thought fly fast. the lady herself

should cure the boy. he would see to that. if he couldn’t break an Edna

Donnithorpe, bring she to heel, he be not John Baltazar. in his

jealousy for the boy’s honourable career he sweep the woman’s possible

emotion into the limbo of inconsiderable thing. what kind of a woman

be she, anyhow, to have marry a rat like Donnithorpe? he read she in

rough intolerance. just a freak of thwarted sex. that be it. if nothing

be discover, she would return to her normal life and, size up the

episode in her cold intellectual way, would discover that the game be

not worth the candle supply by the old woman in the remote cottage,

and would send Godfrey pack to any kind of byronic despair. if the

intrigue come out and there be a divorce and subsequent marriage, there

would be the devil to pay.



the taxi clatter through the gloomy archway approach at Waterloo and

draw up at the end of the long line of cab at the entrance to the

station. the summer exodus from London be just begin, and the

outside platform be a-bustle with porter, truck, passenger and

luggage. Baltazar, after pay his fare, linger for a moment at the

great door of the Booking Hall, and then enter and pass through it

into the hurrying station. a queue stand at the suburban ticket office.

he scan it, but no Godfrey. he walk the length of the platform

entrance, through the crowd of passenger and their dump of luggage

and knot of soldier, some about to entrain, sit on the ground with

their pack around they, other, newly arrive on leave: australian

with their soft hat, wiry Cockneys still encase in the clay of the

trench, officer of all grade and of all arm. presently at the

central bookstall, turn away, his arm full of periodical, Godfrey

come into view. Baltazar approach smile. his son’s face darken. “I

don’t expect to see you here, sir.”



“if you want to study the way of a country, there’s nothing like its

great railway station. they’re a favourite haunt of mine.”



“it’s rather stuffy under this glass roof, don’t you think?” say

Godfrey.



“I don’t mind it, my boy,” reply Baltazar cheerfully. “but it’s lucky

I hit upon Waterloo. I shall be able to see you off. by the way, where

be you go?”



“Somewhere Southampton way, sir,” say Godfrey stiffly.



“lot of light literature,” remark Baltazar, motion to the

periodical.



“quite a debauch,” say Godfrey.



Baltazar’s quick eye pick out the board by the Southampton platform.



“your train, I see, go at 5.45. you’re a bit early.”



“yes, sir. it’s such a long time till the train start that I couldn’t

think of ask you to wait.”



“that don’t matter a bit, my dear boy. time be no object.”



“I’m very sorry to be rude, sir—but as a matter of fact I have an

appointment,” say Godfrey desperately. “an important appointment.”



“oh!” say Baltazar.



“and, if you don’t mind, I must wait outside the station. Quong Ho be

bring my suit-case. I shouldn’t like to miss he.”



he make a step forward, but an ironic glitter in his father’s search

eye arrest the movement.



“Quong Ho ben’t bring your suit-case. I’ve come instead.”



Godfrey draw himself up haughtily. “I don’t understand. have you be

kind enough to bring my luggage?”



“no,” reply Baltazar calmly. “it’s on the floor of the dining-room.”



“your interference with my arrangement, sir, be unwarrantable,” say

the boy, pale with anger.



“possibly. unless we adopt the Jesuitical principle of the end

justify the mean.”



“and what be the end, might I ask?”



“to prevent you from make an infernal fool of yourself.”



the young man regard he inimically. Baltazar feel a throb of pride in

his attitude. a lad of spirit.



“I suppose Marcelle come straight to you with my confidence. in give

it to she I make a fool of myself, I admit. as for what I propose to do,

I fail to see that it’s any concern of your.”



Baltazar’s heart yearn over the boy. he say in a softened tone: “it

be ruin to your career and a mess up of your whole life. and your future

mean so much to I that I’d sacrifice anything—honour, decency, even

your affection which I think I have gain—to see you off at any rate

to France with a clean sheet.”



but Godfrey in cold wrath do not heed the pleading note. he have be

betray and trick. only his soldier’s training keep he outwardly

calm. to the casual glance of the preoccupied crowd pass by they

nothing in the demeanour of either man give occasion for special

interest. they stand, too, in a little islet of space apart from the

general stream of traffic. Baltazar go on with his parable. he have not

the heart to hint his project gibe at the unromantic lack of

tooth-brush. thing run too deep.



“I admit none of your argument,” say Godfrey at last. “besides, I be

my own master. I owe you a debt for many kindness; your affection—I

don’t undervalue it. but there thing end. after all, we meet a year ago

as stranger. I’ve run my life as I choose, and I mean to run it as I

choose. I expect Lady Edna to arrive at any minute. in common delicacy I

must ask you to let I go my own way.”



“all right, go,” say Baltazar. “but I’ll go with you.”



Godfrey’s eye flame.



“you wouldn’t dare!”



“my dear fellow,” say Baltazar, “I don’t think there’s a damned thing

in the world that I wouldn’t dare. haven’t you find that out?”



so they stand there for a while long, talk in their islet beneath

the glass roof of the busy station, and the boy’s heart be fill with

anger and wild hatred of the thick-shoulder, smile man, with the

powerful face and infernal dancing eye.



then suddenly Baltazar stride away at a great pace, and Godfrey,

turning, see that he be cut off Lady Edna, who have enter,

precede by a porter wheel her luggage. before he have time to

“of course.”



he march away across the station.



“Porter——” say Lady Edna.

“I’ve naturally count on the consequence of your resentment,” say

he follow her stare across the station, and there, in the archway of
