                             CHAPTER XXIII





“you seem to have manage your little affair rather clumsily,” say

“probably catch you and Godfrey.”

Baltazar throw up his hand. “oh, Lord! the usual idiocy. for a clever

use your brain. don’t say a word to give yourself away.”

“I’ll see,” say he.

Baltazar hesitate. should he or should he not return to Lady Edna? if

“ah, Donnithorpe!”

he be enjoy himself amazingly. Donnithorpe, baffle, tug at his

the porter wheel off the luggage. Lady Edna turn to follow, but she

“not yet.”

but Donnithorpe smile his thin, derisive smile. “no. they’re too

the solicitous porter, already reward with five shilling, and

Baltazar let himself into the house in Sussex Gardens, and go straight

“write to she, I suppose.”

“where be you go to address it?”

it be a cosy room at the back of the house, the smoking den of the late

“Quong Ho be sure that he want you.”

I.”



there be a long pause, during which Baltazar bend his disconcerting and

“Godfrey,” he say at last, “what make you such an infatuated fool as to

“what do you mean?”



and then, when Baltazar describe the disastrous paper, he cry

but Baltazar hold he with his inscrutable eye.



“you’re a brilliant soldier, my son, but you’re no match for a foxy old

“what the devil be I to do?” ask Godfrey with a helpless gesture.



Baltazar rise. “my boy,” say he, “in two or three day’ time they’re

in spite of the welter of disillusion and catastrophe in which the boy

Baltazar put his arm round his son’s shoulder very tenderly.



“my boy,” say he, “I’d give my life for you.” and the young man hung

his head. “the only thing be, will you trust I?”



ten minute afterwards Baltazar, cheery and confident, stand at the door

prepare to depart from a chasten though more hopeful Godfrey. love

have conquer. what have pass between his father and the Donnithorpes

the boy do not know. of his father’s assumption of the part of

dominate his will, evoke in he a blind, unquestione confidence,

compel from he a promise of implicit obedience. of course there be

condition. he be to petition the War Office to be allow to sacrifice

his father say, be bind by the same condition. . . . Baltazar stand

by the door.



“it’s all damn hard, old man, I know. but you’ll worry through. it’s

the english way.”



he walk out, hum “Tipperary” out of tune, the only modern air he

know, and ascend the stair and thrust his head into the drawing-room.

there, as he expect, he find a desolate Marcelle, who, throw down

the book which she be try to read, jump up and run to the door.

what have happen? Quong Ho have tell she of Edgar Donnithorpe’s call.

Godfrey be in black anger against she.



“go down,” say he, “and make your peace with he. you’ll stay and dine.

I must go now and finish my work before dinner.”



he leave she and, still hum “Tipperary,” enter his library, where

“Miss Baring and Captain Godfrey have upbraid I for indiscretion in

that I inform Mr. Donnithorpe of your whereabouts,” say Quong Ho.



“the good day’s work you ever do in your life,” say Baltazar, seat

himself at the table and take up his pen.



                 *        *        *        *        *



the dinner be not quite the success for which Baltazar have hope, in

spite of his effort to set a tone of light-hearted gaiety. his good

champagne flow to little purpose. Godfrey acknowledge the toast to

his promotion and appointment with irreproachable politeness and

lamentable lack of fervour. Marcelle confess afterwards that she have

never sit through so unjoyous a meal. to make her peace with Godfrey have

be no easy matter. it be but an armistice that she have patch up.

twice that day have he be betray by woman, and he feel sore against

an untrustworthy sex. he have admit she not an inch far into his

confidence. of the incriminate scrap of paper he tell she nothing. she

sit at the table puzzle and unhappy. Quong Ho eat philosophically when

he be not drink in the word of wisdom that come from the master’s

lip.



they break up early. Godfrey retire to his room. Quong Ho depart to

the printer to correct the proof of the editorial. Baltazar walk home

with Marcelle: a somewhat silent and miserable little journey. in vain

he assure she that she have be Godfrey’s salvation. she only realize

that the boy’s faith in she have go. of the extent of the salvation he,

forthrightness scorn half confidence. he walk back disappointed,

ever so little depressed. hadn’t he tell everybody to put their trust in

he and worry their head no more about the matter? and they be

worry considerably.



at the end of the passage beyond the hall he see a streak of light

signify that Godfrey’s door be ajar. he go down, open the door

and look in. there be Godfrey, huddle up on the Chesterfield, his

head in his hand, his finger clutch his crisp fair hair. as he

seem unaware of intrusion, Baltazar close the door quietly and

tiptoe away. no one know well than he that every man must go through

his little Gethsemane alone. but the pity of it! he creep upstairs with

an aching heart. paper by the last post in connection with the new

ministry lie on his desk. he sit down and try to deal with they; but

at last abandon they and suck a gloomy pipe. have he save the boy

after all? would the woman hold her tongue? be Donnithorpe such a fool

as to believe his story? meanwhile he be the avow lover of the

detest woman and the betrayer of official secret. and the vindictive

“I think, sir, you’re the good father that ever a man have.”



and Baltazar, with gladness leap into his eye and a grin on his

“God know I try to be.”

“no,” say Baltazar in his grand self-confidence. “damn lawyer.”

he be show into a room where Edgar Donnithorpe and an impassive

                              CHAPTER XXIV

    “my dear boy:



    I think you ought to know that I have be as good as my word.

                              CHAPTER XXV





as he have expect, the Foreign Office beam on he. it be immensely

the first announcement in an evening newspaper of his retirement from

her throat be dry. she get out of bed and drink a glass of water. on

and the brass Yale latchkey lie mockingly within her range of vision.



                 *        *        *        *        *



Baltazar walk home, her last word echo in his ear. his absence in

he enter his house in Sussex Gardens remorseful for lack of

he be fill his pipe when Quong Ho enter the library with his

“Sir,” say he, “may I be allow to commit an indiscretion?”

“in high chinese circle in London it be common knowledge,” reply

Quong Ho.



“together with lot of other thing concern I, I suppose.”



“you have many time observe,” say Quong Ho, “that my countryman be

afflict with an abnormal thirst for unessential information.”



in spite of his heavy-heartedness, Baltazar smile grimly.



“well, suppose I be go to China. what of it?”



“may I postpone Cambridge degree and Fellowship for several year and

accompany you?”



Baltazar’s brow grow black. “ben’t england good enough for you?”



Quong Ho break into florid Chinese, the only vehicle for his emotion.

England be the land of his dream. but why should he lie beneath the

passion-flower of luxury while his master eat the bread of exile? surely

his degraded unworthiness might be useful to his illustrious Excellency

as confidential secretary not unversed, thank to his honoured master

and patron, in the language and scholarship of the Mandarins. or, if

that be deem too honourable a position, his filial piety ordain

that he should offer himself as slave or any debase instrument for

which use could be find.



“oh, for God’s sake talk English!” cry Baltazar, his nerve on edge,

foresee such endless verbiage in similar perfect phrasing that

await he in China.



Quong Ho spread out his hand and his face grow impassive. “I have

speak,” he reply simply.



“I don’t want any more career upset,” say Baltazar, irritably. “you’re

fix. you’ve to get your Fellowship. you’ll stay in England. besides, I

need you here to look after Miss Baring’s interest.”



“I confess,” say Quong Ho, gravely, “to be oblivious of that side of

the question.”



Baltazar, lie deep in his arm-chair, pipe in mouth, gaze intently

into the oblique steadfast eye of the son of his quaint adoption. the

idea of leave Marcelle under his protection do not seem in the least

comic. he pass an impatient hand over his brow. be he lose his

sense of value?



apart from his intellectual gift, Quong Ho be a man of shrewd common

sense and of infinite trustworthiness. Marcelle know this. unlike so

many untravelled Englishwomen, she do not regard a Chinaman as a sort

of dangerous toy dog. she share his faith in Quong Ho.



“I thank you for your offer, my dear fellow,” he say at last, repent

his ungraciousness. “I know you make it out of affection for I. I

deeply appreciate it. if it ben’t for Miss Baring, I wouldn’t

hesitate. as it be, I leave you here as my agent.”



Quong Ho bow. “so long as I can be of service to you, sir, your word

be law,” say he, and retire.



Baltazar, leave alone, resume his uninspired reflection. he feel

physically and morally weary, a beat man. he shrink from his chinese

exile with pathetic dread; shrink from the toilsome journey, the

eternal compliment of convention that delay serious discussion, the

perpetual ceremonial, the futile tea-drinking, the mass of tradition and

prejudice and ignorance, the smile craft that use it as a buffer

against enlightenment. he look with dismay on his exclusion from the

keen intellectual talk in which he have revel for the past year, from

the brain-thrilling battle of Western Thought. it be a man’s work, his

mission; a pick man’s work. hundred would have regard it as a

climax of their diplomatic ambition. but to he, who have throw himself

into vast scheme for the reconstruction of the war-tear world, it be

exile, defeat. it be not in his nature to regret his sacrifice. what

be do be do. the star in their course have fight against he

individually, even though, in their inscrutable wisdom they fight, as

he believe, for his House. no man who have saturate himself for year

with chinese thought can escape the spiritual influence of fatalism. he

be a fatalist. it be write that he should fail in every one of his

great adventure. yet the fact of it be write make his lot none the

less damnable for the very human and vivid man, once more involve in

predestine shipwreck.



he smoke many pipe think disconnectedly, without method, and

feel old and lonely and break, and very, very tired. at last his

pipe drop to the floor and he fall asleep.



suddenly the subconsciousness of a presence in the room cause he to

awake with a start. he look up and, bewildered, see Marcelle stand

by his chair. she be cry. he spring to his foot, pass his hand

over his eye.



“you here?” his glance instinctively seek the clock on the

mantelpiece. “why, it’s half-past two in the morning!”



she say: “I couldn’t sleep. I couldn’t rest. I have to come.”



he do not understand.



“what be the matter, my dearest? what can I do for you?”



“only go on love I, and forgive I,” she say desperately.



“but I do,” he cry, puzzle. “it’s just hell for I to leave you. but

I cann’t help it, my dear. my hand have be force. it’s even hard to

leave you than it be twenty year ago. I love you and want you more

than ever I do in my life.”



“so do I,” she say, in a shake voice. “that’s why I’m here, at

half-past two in the morning.”



Baltazar utter a great triumphant cry and clasp she in his arm.



“my God,” say he, “I’ve win after all!”



he hold she at arm’s length and look at she exultantly. thank Heaven

she have no suspicion of his sense of downfall. not Pity, but love at

last awaken, have bring she to he.



“yes,” he repeat. “I’ve win after all.”



after a while, when he have almost forget his word, she ask he:



“what do you think you have lose?”



“my faith in my destiny. the star of Baltazar. once upon a time the

original bearer of my name, with the other, have faith in a star, and he

follow it and find God.”



she smile. “dear, ben’t you talk a bit wildly?”



“what’s the good of speech if one cann’t use it wildly in wild moment?”

he laugh. “oh, you beloved woman,” say he, and kiss she.



presently: “you’ll come out to China with I? you’ll progress like a

queen. I’ll see to that.”



“it don’t matter how I progress,” she say, “so long as I’m with you.

I’m yours body and soul to the end of time.”



“to the end of eternity,” he cry. “I prefer that. it’s big. the

big there be be good enough for I.”



his dancing eye burn like flame of pride and happiness. twenty year

seem to have fall from he, and she see before she the young man

whom as a girl she have love.



“you and I be go over to the great work ever attempt by man.

the regeneration of half the continent of Asia. I couldn’t have do it

alone. the prospect frighten I. yes, it do. I haven’t the heart. but

with you—I stake my faith in the Star—it’ll be one of the great

accomplishment of the war. Quong Ho will come with we. he’ll have his

chance. I’ll make he one of the great man of the New China.”



he go on, expound his vision of the new order of oriental thing.

she marvel at he, for it seem as if he have but live for that

moment.



and divine his Great Sacrifice, she forget the selfless year that have

all but mould she into a mere machine of tender service to maim and

diseased humanity, and feel a thing of small account before this man

whose unconquerable faith and indomitable courage transform his

colossal vanity into virtue, and who, for all his egotism, be

endow with the supreme gift of love.



“Godfrey will be astonish at all this,” she hazard.



“Astonishment,” say he, “be an emotion salutary for the very young. it

stimulate think.”



                                the END
